- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/349999/][Illustrating the Linux sock_sendpage() NULL pointer dereference]]: Ramon de Carvalho Valle released exploit for Tavis Ormandy's sock_sendpage() NULL pointer vulnerability. Exploits mmap_min_addr bypass via SELinux policy on RHEL/CentOS 5.x (fixed versions not vulnerable). Affects 2.4.4-2.4.37.4 and 2.6.0-2.6.30.4. Tested on RHEL 4.8/5.3, CentOS 4.8/5.3, SUSE, Ubuntu. Fix committed by Linus Aug 13, 2009; mmap_min_addr > 0 mitigates.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/349970/][Ext3 and RAID: silent data killers?]]: Jonathan Corbet examines Pavel Machek's documentation patch on ext3/RAID data loss risks. Flash drive firmware corruption can trash unrelated blocks during write — journaling can't protect. RAID5 degraded mode + power loss during write corrupts stripe data silently; fsck doesn't catch collateral damage. Ric Wheeler: easiest data loss is enabled write cache. Solutions: disable write cache + enable barriers, don't remove flash until writes complete, degraded arrays vulnerable. No substitute for backups.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351263/][Netboot.me turns netboot into internetboot]]: Service allowing PXE boot of various Linux distros and FreeBSD over the internet via gPXE. Users download 1MB image to USB/CD, boot to retrieve menu of available OS installers (Debian, Fedora, openSUSE, Ubuntu, FreeBSD) plus live CDs and rescue tools (GParted, Memtest86). Uses chainload URLs identifying kernel, initrd, and kernel arguments. Hackable and open for custom configurations. Security concerns: no certificate verification in gPXE SSL, poor random number generator; RSA signing proposed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351532/][FUD at Best Buy]]: Microsoft training materials for Best Buy sales staff containing anti-Linux FUD exposed. Claims: no support, long maintenance time, no regular updates, no tutorials. Omits facts: World of Warcraft runs on Linux via WINE, cameras work fine, printers improving. Community debates hardware support reality — some argue Linux still has usability gaps for non-technical users; others counter that many issues stem from low-end hardware and help-desk unfamiliarity. Microsoft sees Linux as competitive threat requiring response.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351013/][Debian switching to upstart]]: Petter Reinholdtsen announced Debian's plan to replace sysvinit with upstart for event-based boot system. Solves fundamental race condition problems: /dev entries missing when fsck runs, network unavailable for NFS mounts, device detection timing issues. Dependency-based boot sequencing (already default in Debian unstable) is step one; replacing /sbin/init with upstart is step two for Squeeze. Provides parallel service startup and smarter boot based on kernel events. Canonical's upstart already used by Ubuntu and Fedora.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/352831/][A new open source foundation]]: CodePlex Foundation announcement — Microsoft-sponsored organization to promote commercial participation in free software. skepticism from community due to Microsoft funding and Sam Ramji (former Microsoft open source lead) as interim president. Board has 3 Microsoft employees of 6; advisory board has 6 Microsoft employees of 12. Lawyer Andy Updegrove analyzes by-laws: no membership organization, interim board elects permanent board with 4-year terms, 2/3 supermajority required for bylaw changes (two board members can veto). Contribution agreements grant broad patent rights to foundation and downstream. Critics see this as Microsoft creating controlled playing field; supporters see potential for improved Microsoft-open source relations.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/352366/][FOSS license compliance in the consumer electronics market]]: Analysis of FOSS license compliance problems in CE devices — primarily economic rather than dishonest. Consumer electronics sold in high volumes for low margins; ODMs develop products for competing western companies using single board designs. Issues: incomplete source code from chip vendors, customized source trees not fully reintegrated, missing license texts in manuals. Compliance engineering adds ~€6/unit cost which may eliminate profitability for small runs of 200 devices. Companies face choice of shipping non-compliant software or missing market windows. Market timing critical; 3-month sales window dominates. Gpl-violations.org and SFLC have improved compliance enforcement. Recommendation: document violations carefully, contact copyright holders, be fair and professional in enforcement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353970/][LinuxCon: Secure virtualization with sVirt]]: Red Hat's Dan Walsh presented sVirt — applying SELinux mandatory access controls to restrict guest actions even if they break out of containment. Running multiple guests on same hardware is "one of scariest things you can do" from security standpoint. Hypervisor vulnerabilities are attacker's #1 goal. sVirt dynamically labels VMs using MCS fields in SELinux; when guest exits, image relabeled back to original. virt-manager handles automatic relabeling starting with Fedora 11. Also introduced sandbox -X combining sandbox with xguest to sandbox arbitrary desktop applications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353203/][Walsh: Cool things with SELinux... Introducing sandbox -X]]: Dan Walsh's new SELinux sandbox feature combines sandbox with xguest approach to create sandboxes for arbitrary desktop applications. Requested to sandbox Acroread — which accesses config files, uses GConf, X server, other apps, and has full run of home directory. No good general-purpose way existed to lock down such applications without breaking them.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353879/][Why open-source DNS is 'internet's dirty little secret' (ZDNet)]]: ZDNet interview with Nominum's Jon Shalowitz pushing commercial DNS — claims open source makes code visible to hackers, cannot keep secrets. Described as "amusingly retro 1990's-style security FUD."
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353411/][Log-structured file systems: There's one in every SSD]]: Valerie Aurora article explaining SSDs internally use log-structured file system techniques (wear-leveling, write-gathering via flash translation layer). TRIM support is crucial but currently poorly implemented — TRIM commands untagged and some SSDs take hundreds of milliseconds to process. Without TRIM, SSDs accumulate "zombie" blocks that can't be reused. File systems should implement proper TRIM/garbage collection.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353837/][AppArmor: it's baaaaaaack]]: John Johansen (Canonical) posted new AppArmor patches at LinuxCon. AppArmor had difficult path into mainline — pathname-based approach concerned developers, core developers lost jobs and moved on. TOMOYO Linux breaking barriers helped. AppArmor uses new security module hooks added for TOMOYO. Chances of merger should be better now.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353849/][Devtmpfs and permissions]]: Ingo Molnar reported bug — devtmpfs created /dev/null and /dev/zero inaccessible to unprivileged accounts, breaking most applications. devtmpfs developers originally said udev should set permissions, but devtmpfs can now run without udev. Linus agreed some policy must be in kernel. devtmpfs now queries kernel subsystems for default permissions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353826/][The Orocos Project - an open-source robotics library]]: OROCOS (Open Robot Control Software) is collection for robotics — Real-Time Toolkit (RTT), Kinematics and Dynamics Library (KDL), Bayesian Filtering Library (BFL), Orocos Component Library. LGPL+GPL with runtime exception. Applied to Blender mill interface, autonomous automobile, EasyOROCOS CAD.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/350352/][A trojan for Skype]]: Windows trojan extracts Skype voice calls as MP3s and ships them elsewhere. While Linux is not directly threatened, highlights privacy concerns about Skype — closed source, obfuscation techniques, rumored government backdoors. Discussion notes difficulty of reverse-engineering Skype protocol and implications for free alternatives like Ekiga which lack interoperability.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/350219/][O_*SYNC]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Linux synchronous I/O flags (O_SYNC, O_DSYNC, O_RSYNC) which were never properly implemented. Christoph Hellwig working on proper implementation for 2.6.32. Issues: Linux has always lied about O_SYNC (actually giving O_DSYNC), and open() ignores unknown flags creating compatibility problems. Solution: internally O_SYNC becomes O_DSYNC with hidden O_FULLSYNC flag for full semantics, glibc defines O_SYNC as (O_FULLSYNC|O_DSYNC).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/350123/][The offline scheduler]]: Jake Edge covers Raz Ben-Yehuda offline scheduler patch removing CPUs from kernel control via hot-unplug for undisturbed code execution. Main objections: bypasses Linux entirely, only runs kernel-context not user-space, cpusets already provide CPU partitioning. Ingo Molnar/Thomas Gleixner suggest dynamic scheduler tick alternative (partially implemented 2.6.26). Offline scheduler unlikely mainline.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351053/][The Grumpy Editor hugin experience]]: Jonathan Corbet reviews hugin panorama tool — handles lens distortion/parallax, tested on Colorado photos. US users lose auto control-point feature due to SIFT patent; autopano-sift-C from rpmfusion dramatically improves experience. Also useful for perspective correction on single images. Positive: unique free software for complex image manipulation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351263/][Netboot.me turns netboot into internetboot]]: Nick Johnson service using gPXE to PXE boot distros over internet. 1MB image to USB/CD gives menu of OS installers (Debian, Fedora, openSUSE, Ubuntu, FreeBSD) plus live CDs and rescue tools (GParted, Memtest86). Hackable with custom configs. Security: no certificate verification in gPXE SSL, poor random number generator; RSA signing proposed. Compare to boot.kernel.org (BKO). BSD license, runs on Google App Engine.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351499/][BFS vs CFS scheduler comparison]]: Con Kolivas introduced BFS (Brain Fuck Scheduler), a new CPU scheduler targeting desktop systems. Ingo Molnar responded with benchmarks showing BFS performed worse than CFS. Key insight: latency parameters can be tuned on CFS for better interactivity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351480/][Staging tree status for 2.6.32]]: Greg Kroah-Hartman provided a staging tree status update for 2.6.32. Staging contains 40+ drivers meant to be cleaned up for mainline inclusion.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351422/][POSIX filesystem reality gap]]: Explores the gap between POSIX filesystem specifications and reality, focusing on the fsync()/rename() controversy and data durability after crashes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/350969/][Thurman: Writing apps for the N900, part 1]]: Thomas Thurman started a series on writing GTK applications for the N900 device. Two key considerations: widgets that don't exist on desktop because they work better on phones, and an ecosystem of programs that must be compatible with.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/351225/][Thurman: Writing apps for the N900, part 2 - packaging]]: Thomas Thurman continued his series on GTK apps for N900, covering packaging issues. Clarified Qt apps run under Maemo 5 and GTK apps will still run under Maemo 6.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/352432/][Writing kernel modules in Haskell]]: Instructions appeared for writing Linux kernel modules in Haskell using modified GHC. Example code: `hello = newCString "hello" >>= printk >> return 0`. Community debate about garbage collection in kernel modules - many argue GC latency makes it impractical.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/352746/][Van de Ven: Introducing 'timechart']]: Arjan van de Ven introduced timechart, a new tool based on perf to visualize and diagnose latency problems in Linux. Output is "infinitely zoomable."
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353044/][Video buffer pools]]: Laurent Pinchart proposed a new subsystem for global video buffer pools in Video4Linux2 to solve latency problems with large contiguous buffer allocations. Buffers allocated early, cache invalidation done ahead of time.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/352863/][Various scheduler-related topics]]: Covered BFS discussion, NEW_FAIR_SLEEPERS flag (disabled in 2.6.32), child-runs-first changed to parent-runs-first for kernel builds, and improved cpuidle governor by Arjan van de Ven for better power management.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353050/][Hw-breakpoint: shared debugging registers]]: K. Prasad, Frederic Weisbecker, and Alan Stern developed hw-breakpoint API for multiple debuggers (kgdb, gdb) to share hardware breakpoint registers without conflict. Integrated into perfcounters.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354408/][LPC: 25 years of X]]: Keith Packard keynote at Linux Plumbers Conference reviewing X11 history — MIT license success, lessons learned from design decisions. X has been foundational to free software graphics despite controversies over extension complexity and rendering architecture.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354387/][FOSS compliance engineering in the embedded industry]]: gpl-violations.org announced compliance engineering services for embedded industry — binary analysis tools, license scanning, compliance documentation. Helps companies navigate GPL/LGPL obligations.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354897/][BruCON: Can we trust cryptography?]]: Vincent Rijmen keynote on broken crypto algorithms — A5/1 GSM encryption cracked, KeeLoq car keys broken, WEP WiFi devastated. Proposed "green cryptography" methodology for evaluating algorithm security before deployment.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354861/][Featherstitch: Killing fsync() softly]]: Valerie Aurora presented Featherstitch patch interface for kernel block layer — patchgroups allow batching fsync() calls, dramatically reducing I/O overhead while maintaining durability. Userspace API enables applications to group related metadata updates.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354690/][The realtime preemption mini-summit]]: Jonathan Corbet covered RT preemption discussions — threaded IRQs, handling SMIs (System Management Interrupts), BKL removal progress, signal delivery latency, and scalability concerns for larger systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354664/][Linux-RT for Debian]]: Pengutronix announced official real-time Linux kernel packages for Debian — APT-compatible RT kernel images, bridging embedded RT needs with Debian infrastructure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354893/][Designing Social Interfaces]]: O'Reilly book announcement covering social interface design patterns — principles for building community-oriented applications with practical examples and case studies.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354624/][Learning Python (4th edition)]]: Multiple Python learning books announced 4th editions — Mark Lutz Learning Python and Programming Python (O'Reilly), David Beazley Python Essential Reference (Addison-Wesley). Comprehensive updates for Python 3.x migration.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354239/][Is Linux Code Quality Improving?]]: Coverity scan report — Linux defect density reduced 16% year-over-year, 0.61 defects per 1000 lines. Positive trend but kernel still shows more defects than average codebase.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354899/][Updegrove: CodePlex Foundation reflections]]: Andy Updegrove analyzed CodePlex Foundation governance — Microsoft initiative for open source projects at codeplex.com. Questions about patent commitments and open governance compared to Apache Foundation model.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/355904/][The CFQ "low latency" mode]]: New CFQ I/O scheduler mode for desktop responsiveness — reduces latency for interactive workloads by favoring sequential request completion over throughput, implemented via target latencies per process.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/355934/][The ACPI processor aggregator driver]]: New driver implementing ACPIProcessor Aggregator interface — allows idle CPUs to be put in deeper C-states via emergency realtime thread, part of power management improvements.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/355700/][Concurrency-managed workqueues]]: Tejun Heo introduced new workqueue design replacing per-CPU dedicated threads with thread pools — improves scalability, simplifies code, enables automatic load balancing across CPUs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/354769/][Infrastructure unification in the block layer]]: Neil Brown explored challenges unifying Device Mapper and Software RAID — different abstractions, bio handling, personality differences make merging problematic without significant API redesign.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/355542/][LPC: The past, present, and future of Linux audio]]: Paul Davis and Lennart Poettering discussed audio stack evolution — PulseAudio vs JACK debates, Pro Audio working group progress, JackAudioKit, and challenges of low-latency audio on Linux.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/356776/][On the driver life cycle]]: Greg Kroah-Hartman explained staging tree philosophy — unmaintained drivers live in staging as last resort before removal, requires demonstrable use case and commitment to eventual cleanup.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/356899/][Char devices for network interfaces]]: Dell proposed patch for persistent network interface naming — udev rules to create char devices for network interfaces, enabling reliable naming regardless of boot order.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/356378/][Fixing kmap_atomic()]]: Peter Zijlstra replaced kmap_atomic fixed slots with stack-based implementation — eliminates slot exhaustion on NUMA systems, simplifies code, removes arbitrary slot limits.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/356890/][Ask a kernel developer, part 2]]: Greg Kroah-Hartman answered questions on kernel development — how to contact maintainers, appropriate use of security@kernel.org, staging tree expectations, regression handling.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/356576/][Deadline scheduling for Linux]]: Dario Faggioli presented EDF (Earliest Deadline First) scheduler as SCHED_DEADLINE — bandwidth-preserving algorithm ensuring tasks meet deadlines, uses timed interrupt to preempt.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/356974/][The Book of Xen]]: No Starch Press announced Xen virtualization book — comprehensive guide to Xen hypervisor covering setup, configuration, security, and advanced topics.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/357774/][Thunderbird and Fedora]]: Nathan Willis covered Thunderbird update controversy — Fedora 13 shipped Thunderbird 3 without proper karma approval, Bodhi karma system's limitations exposed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/359046/][Tracefs]]: Greg Kroah-Hartman created tracefs filesystem from debugfs — dedicated to tracing infrastructure, cleaner separation of concerns, new mount point for trace filesystems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/359219/][/proc and directory permissions]]: Security issue with /proc file descriptors — improper permission checks allowed local privilege escalation, fd directory accessible despite restricted permissions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/358910/][JLS2009: Generic receive offload]]: Herbert Xu explained GRO for 10Gb Ethernet — coalesces network packets at receive path, reduces CPU overhead, significant performance improvement for high-speed networking.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/359158/][Transparent hugepages]]: Andrea Arcangeli presented transparent hugepage support — automatically uses 2MB pages where beneficial, hugetlbfs integration without manual management, reduces TLB pressure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/357767/][File holes, races, and mmap()]]: Goldwyn Rodrigues contributed article on filesystem races between mmap() and truncate() — Jan Kara patch introduces block_prepare_hole()/block_finish_hole() to serialize hole creation during page faults, preventing data loss and stray non-zeroes in sparse files.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353641/][DragonFly BSD Release 2.4]]: DragonFly BSD 2.4 release — three ISO options (bare-bones CD, DVD with X environment, bootable USB), first 64-bit ISO offered. Notable for HAMMER filesystem rivaling ZFS in features and stability.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/353644/][Mandriva Linux 2010 RC1 is now available]]: Mandriva Linux 2010 RC1 release candidate — hybrid ISOs work on both CD and USB, bugfix-focused with some major updates, available via Mandriva-seeds for easy testing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/359489/][Gerrit: Google-style code review meets git]]: Don Marti article on Gerrit code review system — Google-style tool for Android using companies (HTC, Qualcomm, TI, Sony Ericsson, Google). Based on Mondrian, uses JGit, GWT web interface, OpenID auth. Provides multi-level approval, Change-Id for version tracking, email notifications. Used to gate Android code contributions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/359992/][The Python: Rag]]: November 2009 edition of Python: Rag magazine — PDF format aimed at beginners and veterans, published monthly.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/359998/][Toward a smarter OOM killer]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Hiroyuki Kamezawa's OOM killer improvements — uses RSS instead of total_vm, tracks swap usage, improved fork bomb detection (5-minute window), focuses on processes expanding memory recently vs long-running processes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360040/][Wheeler: Fully Countering Trusting Trust through Diverse Double-Compiling]]: David Wheeler's PhD dissertation defense on countering Ken Thompson's "Trusting Trust" compiler attack — Diverse Double-Compiling (DDC) detects maliciously corrupted compilers. Formal proof of effectiveness, GCC demonstration, independent compiler comparison.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360199/][JLS: Increasing VFS scalability]]: Nick Piggin's Japan Linux Symposium talk on VFS scalability — five bottlenecks addressed: files_lock (per-CPU lists), vfsmount_lock (brlocks), mnt_count (per-CPU), dcache_lock (split locking), inode_lock (per-CPU inode allocation). Showed 450→300,000 ops/sec improvement on 64 CPUs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360328/][Another null pointer exploit]]: Race condition in kernel pipe code (CVE-2009-3546) — closing pipe before open completes causes NULL pointer dereference. Fix makes code check pipe status before opening. 34 null pointer bugs fixed since 2.6.31. Recommends vm.mmap_min_addr protection.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360347/][Deprecating IDE?]]: Robert Hancock patch to mark IDE as deprecated in 2.6.33 — most distributions already use libata PATA. David Miller requires libata to create /dev/hdX names first and pmac driver support before deprecation proceeds.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360432/][Strandboge: AppArmor sVirt security driver for libvirt]]: Jamie Strandboge announced AppArmor support for sVirt/libvirt 0.7.2 — on par with SELinux driver feature support. Ubuntu 9.10 includes it. Submitted to Linux LSM.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360587/][Next-generation Linux file systems: NiLFS(2) and exofs]]: IBM developerWorks introduction to log-structured filesystems — NiLFS(2) uses continuous checkpointing, garbage collection for disk space. exofs is exoscale object storage filesystem. LFS issues with fragmentation and cleaning discussed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360699/][A futex overview and update]]: Darren Hart's comprehensive futex article — covers futex fundamentals, PI futexes, robust futexes, private futexes (per-process), adaptive spinning, bitset conditional wakeup, requeue_PI patches for glibc condvars.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360847/][Perl far from dead, more popular than you think]]: Royal Pingdom article on Perl usage — Perl still powers many big sites despite perception it's dying. Active in bioinformatics, system administration, web (BBC iPlayer, Craigslist, Ticketmaster). CPAN ecosystem strength, Moose OO framework discussed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360955/][Another new ABI for fanotify]]: Eric Paris's fanotify redesign — replaces setsockopt() with fanotify_init() and fanotify_mark() syscalls. Provides filesystem event notification for malware scanning, hierarchical storage. Missing ability to block open() calls.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/361453/][Removing binary sysctl]]: Eric Biederman's patch removes sysctl() syscall implementation — adds compatibility wrapper using /proc/sys instead. Reduces code size, maintains ABI compatibility. Concerns about /proc/sys performance and configuration options.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/360958/][The block I/O controller]]: Vivek Goyal's proportional-weight I/O controller in CFQ scheduler — new blkio cgroup class with I/O weight (100-1000). First step toward multi-level I/O control. Future plans include integration with higher-level controllers for writeback and VM-level throttling.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/361457/][Supporting transactions in btrfs]]: Sage Weil's BTRFS_IOC_USERTRANS ioctl — single syscall for multi-operation transactions. Operations array with open/close/pwrite/unlink/mkdir/truncate/setxattr etc. Doesn't rollback on failure, returns ops_completed. Concerns about syscalls in modules and comparison to syslets.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/361883/][Poll on PyPI rating system]]: Martin v. Löwis announced poll on PyPI rating/comment system — community feedback requested on controversial rating feature.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362175/][Van de Ven: Some PowerTOP updates]]: Arjan van de Ven reported PowerTOP git updates for 2.6.33 — audio and SATA power management improvements, blockdump replacement using perf infrastructure to track disk-waking applications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362179/][High-order GFP_ATOMIC allocation trouble]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Mel Gorman's memory allocation fixes — direct reclaim wake kswapd on failure, congestion wait on both sync/async queues, kswapd catnap instead of immediate sleep, better high-order allocation success rates.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362339/][Receive packet steering]]: Tom Herbert's RPS patch from Google — distributes incoming packet processing across multiple CPUs using hash of protocol data. No driver changes required. e1000: 90K→292K tps, tg3: 90K→285K tps on 8-core. Already running on Google's production servers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362357/][Some approaches to parallelism avoidance]]: Discussion on limiting thread parallelism — sched_wait_block() syscall proposal, Ingo Molnar's perf events approach, Linus's "run only one of group" clone flag. Related to thread pool efficiency and workqueue design.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362371/][eclone()]]: New system call proposal for checkpoint/restart — eclone() with clone_args structure for explicit PID selection in namespaces. Blocked by checkpoint/restart not being ready for mainline.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362377/][Hello, Android, Second Edition]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book announcement — Ed Burnette's Android development book, 2nd edition covering Android 1.5/1.6 (Cupcake/Donut), Sudoku game example, widgets, Android Market publishing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362473/][Reducing HTTP latency with SPDY]]: Nathan Willis article on Google's SPDY protocol — multiplexed streams over SSL, header compression (88% reduction), request prioritization, server push/hint. Up to 60% load time reduction in tests. Alternative to HTTP pipelining.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362803/][Interview: Red Hat on Red Hat Enterprise Virtualization]]: Montana Linux interview with Red Hat's Andy Cathrow and Jim Brennan — RHEV product updates including SAN support (iSCSI/FC), multipath I/O, NIC bonding, VLANs, high availability, SPICE protocol emphasis.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362852/][Debug It!]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book by Paul Butcher on debugging techniques — find, repair, and prevent bugs, empirical approach, reproduction, diagnosis, self-debugging software.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/362864/][RESTful Java with JAX-RS]]: O'Reilly book by Bill Burke — JAX-RS specification for RESTful web services in Java EE6, JBoss RESTEasy implementation, distributed web services design.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363200/][Help wanted: kbuild maintainer]]: Sam Ravnborg stepping down as kbuild maintainer — 3 kids + job left no time. Kbuild "just works" but kconfig select and external module building remain problematic. Seeking replacement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363349/][Videobuf: buffer management for V4L2 drivers]]: Jonathan Corbet's comprehensive Videobuf article — glue layer for V4L2 drivers, supports scatter/gather DMA, vmalloc, and contiguous DMA buffers. Implements read(), poll(), mmap(), streaming I/O ioctls. Documentation to complement kernel source.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363429/][When Designing for Moblin, Think Like a Mobile User]]: Moblin Zone article on mobile UI design — limited attention span, screen real estate, input methods. Concentrate information, avoid excessive notification cascading.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363465/][LPI announces new partner in the Netherlands]]: Linux Professional Institute announces LPI-The Netherlands sub-affiliate — founding partners AT Computing, Ictivity, StarTel, Fontys Hogeschool, Hogeschool Zuyd, NLLGG. Vendor-neutral training and certification emphasis.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363471/][jQuery Cookbook]]: O'Reilly book edited by Cody Lindley — jQuery recipes from 19 developers, UI components, events, effects, optimization, testing, jQuery UI theming.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363474/][Linux Implements Support For Trusted Computing]]: OpenTC project coverage in The Gov Monitor — openSUSE 11.2 implementation, TSS stack, Xen hypervisor improvements, TPM management software. Community debate on TC/DRM implications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363490/][Journal-guided RAID resync]]: Jody McIntyre's journal-guided resync implementation — uses ext3 filesystem journal to track RAID stripe changes, 3-5% performance hit vs 30% for MD write-intent bitmap. Originally from Sun for Lustre, abandoned but patches available for other developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363572/][LogFS returns]]: Jörn Engel's LogFS for solid-state storage returns — flash-optimized log-structured filesystem, format changes complete, seeking merge. Designed for NAND flash, not spinning rust.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/363622/][The Grumpy Editor's Moblin review]]: Jonathan Corbet's review of Moblin on Dell Mini 10v — 27 second boot, MyZone social interface, zones for apps, fast suspend/resume. UI feels "toy-like" with pastel colors. Moblin is Intel's stack including kernel, power management, networking.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364204/][Interstellar overdrive - Linux and astronomy]]: The H article on Linux astronomy software — Celestia 3D space simulation, professional/amateur levels, gravitational wave detection, telescope control.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364386/][How to vote anonymously under ubiquitous surveillance]]: Light Blue Touchpaper on Open Vote Network protocol — decentralized anonymous voting using cryptographic protocols, self-tallying, no central authority needed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364515/][Kernel support for infrared receivers]]: LIRC infrared remote control merging discussion — Jarod Wilson's LIRC patches for mainline, evdev vs raw interface debate, protocol decoding in kernel vs userspace, input subsystem integration. 3rd edition
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364531/][New revision of "Inkscape: Guide to a Vector Drawing Program" book]]: Tavmjong Bah's Inkscape book 3rd edition — covers Inkscape 0.47, available as print and free web PDF.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364572/][The Python: Rag]]: December 2009 Python:Rag newsletter edition — monthly Python programming newsletter.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364583/][Eliminating rwlocks and IRQF_DISABLED]]: Jonathan Corbet on rwlock and interrupt handler changes — tasklist_lock conversion to plain spinlock, fair rwlocks discussion, IRQF_DISABLED removal to run all handlers with interrupts disabled for simplicity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364584/][Another mainline push for utrace]]: Jake Edge covers Oleg Nesterov's utrace patches for 2.6.33 — user-space thread control for debugging/tracing, ptrace() rewrite, SystemTap uses, multiple tracing engines per thread.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364742/][Fault injection and unexpected requirement injection]]: Discussion of futex fault injection patches — Sripathi Kodi's patches rejected by Ingo Molnar suggesting perf events integration instead. Editorial on kernel development process and expanding scope requirements.
#HL 739#A5C#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/364793/][Moving from Python 2 to Python 3]]: Mark Summerfield's 4-page cheat sheet PDF summarizing Python 2↔3 differences and new Python 3.1 features for existing Python 2 programmers wanting to write idiomatic Python 3.
#HL 740#B2D#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365213/][Why Open Source Phones Still Fail]]: PC Magazine article on why open phones fail — mobile carriers subsidize phones creating 2-year lock-ins that make unsubsidized open phones economically uncompetitive ($400 difference). US consumers accept lock-ins for $300 iPhone deals. Europe has more unlocked phones due to regulation requiring compatibility across carriers.
#HL 741#C89#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365224/][SELinux and PostgreSQL]]: Jonathan Corbet covers KaiGai Kohei's SE-PgSQL patch integrating SELinux with PostgreSQL — assigns labels to databases/schemas/rows/columns, evaluates access via SELinux rules. 13,000-line patch (mostly docs/tests) struggling for PostgreSQL mainline acceptance; Tom Lane skeptical of utility, others see interest from military/financial users needing unified security policies across system and database.
#HL 742#D4A#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365443/][2.6.33 merge window part 1]]: Jonathan Corbet covers 2.6.33 merge window changes — ftrace dynamic probes merged, sysctl() binary removed, anticipatory I/O scheduler removed (CFQ only), new block I/O bandwidth controller, TCP cookie transactions, DRBD merged, new drivers (Ralink wireless, Solarflare 10G Ethernet, various audio/CAN/RTC chips).
#HL 743#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365507/][Artifex launches GPL-infringement suit against Palm]]: Artifex (Ghostscript company) sued Palm for using muPDF in Palm Pre without a commercial license — muPDF is GPL-licensed; Palm's PDF viewer is derivative work requiring source release. Palm used GPLv2 version; Artifex offers dual licensing for embedded/hardware products.
