#HL 745#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365674/][LAM Best of mix 2009]]: Linux Audio Musicians annual compilation album of music created with Linux audio tools — released as free download, showcasing Linux audio production capabilities.
#HL 746#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365688/][Announcing fileutils]]: New Python file system library inspired by UNIX commands (cp, mkdir, chmod) — provides intuitive wrappers around os/shutil modules with idempotent operations like mkdir_p.
#HL 747#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365778/][Sugar on a Stick v2 Blueberry released]]: Sugar on a Stick v2 (Blueberry) — Fedora-based portable Sugar learning platform on USB stick, includes Sugar 0.86.3 with tabbed Browse, EPUB Read support, improved wireless/Gnome integration.
#HL 748#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365833/][Minimizing instrumentation impacts]]: Jake Edge covers kprobes jump optimization and jump labels — reduces kprobe overhead from ~1us to ~0.06us using jump instructions instead of breakpoints; jump labels use GCC 4.5 asm goto for tracepoints (2-4 cycle overhead vs no tracepoint).
#HL 749#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365835/][Debugging kernel using Ftrace part 1]]: Steven Rostedt tutorial on Ftrace — covers function tracer, function_graph tracer, trace_printk (low-overhead debug alternative to printk), controlling tracing via tracing_on file, debugfs setup.
#HL 750#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365863/][Spinlock naming resolved]]: Jonathan Corbet — arch_spinlock_t chosen for low-level spinlocks (cannot sleep even in RT kernels), freeing raw_spinlock name for "real" spinlocks in preempt-rt; split allows sleeping spinlocks elsewhere.
#HL 751#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365884/][Kuhn: Anatomy of Modern GPL Violation]]: Bradley Kuhn (SFLC) on GPL violation evolution — from UNIX vendors to embedded devices; community detection makes violations hard to hide; encourages friendly enforcement to bring companies into FLOSS community.
#HL 752#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365916/][First L2Ork track available]]: L2Ork Linux Laptop Orchestra debut recording — "Citadel" piece for soprano and L2Ork; recorded live at Virginia Tech Burruss rotunda without post-processing; posted to L2Ork jukebox.
#HL 753#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/365925/][gnome.org outage]]: Red Hat consolidating GNOME.org servers — 48-hour downtime Dec 12-14 for IP changes; affected www.gnome.org, bugzilla, git, mail servers.
#HL 754#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366480/][Some thoughts on MySQL and Oracle]]: Jonathan Corbet on MySQL/Oracle EU concerns — argues community can fork MySQL if needed; critiques Monty Widenius's re-licensing request as self-serving; discusses corporate open source model risks and copyright assignment dangers.
#HL 755#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366559/][GNOME ponders its code of conduct]]: Jake Edge covers GNOME Foundation discussion on CoC enforcement — debates over policing Planet GNOME content, Richard Stallman's suggestions to bar proprietary software mentions, proposal for private mailing lists for board discussions; most issues handled informally by pgo editors.
#HL 756#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366566/][Kretschmann: Malware Problem]]: Mark Kretschmann on GNOME screensaver malware incident — proposes requiring VCS for Amarok scripts to provide accountability; community discussion on sandboxing approaches (SELinux, NativeClient, VX32) vs user education.
#HL 757#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366648/][The abrupt merging of Nouveau]]: Jonathan Corbet — Fedora's Nouveau driver (reverse-engineered NVIDIA) merged into 2.6.33 after Linus's pressure; ctxprogs binary blob removed via firmware loading API; Red Hat's Ben Skeggs did intensive cleanup work; replacement firmware for GeForce 6/7 announced.
#HL 758#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366679/][Quotes of the week]]: Notable quotes from kernel developers — Dave Airlie on Linus's merge demands, Zachary Amsden on VM complexity, Linus on overdesigning being a sin.
#HL 759#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366717/][RCU mistakes]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Thomas Gleixner's findings on incorrect RCU usage — preempt_disable() no longer sufficient for newer hierarchical RCU; must use rcu_read_lock() instead; Paul McKenney working on lockdep extensions to detect abuse.
#HL 760#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366772/][Power capping]]: Salman Qazi/Google's power capping solution for data centers — forces processor idle for percentage of time based on load; heuristics to target low-priority processes; similar to ACPI processor aggregator driver merged in 2.6.32.
#HL 761#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366796/][Debugging kernel using Ftrace part 2]]: Steven Rostedt tutorial continues — trace_marker for user/kernel synchronization, tracing_on/tracing_off from programs, ftrace_dump_on_oops for crash debugging, stack tracer for finding stack hogs.
#HL 762#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366915/][Redesigning asynchronous suspend/resume]]: Rafael Wysocki's async suspend/resume patches rejected by Linus (overly complex); redesigned using completion structures instead of rwsems; driver-level async decisions; Linus concerned about complexity but agreed to take final version.
#HL 763#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366986/][TCP cookie transactions]]: Jake Edge covers TCPCT merged in 2.6.33 — cryptographically secure cookies in TCP handshake to prevent SYN flood DoS and reduce server state; solves DNSSEC large response problems over UDP; Linux ahead of other OSes in implementation.
#HL 764#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366987/][kmsg_dumper]]: Jonathan Corbet — new mechanism in 2.6.33 to dump kernel log buffer on crash; kmsg_dumper struct with dump() callback receives kernel output; mtdoops module uses it to save crash data to flash.
#HL 765#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/366994/][New per-CPU operations]]: Tejun Heo/Christoph Lameter's new this_cpu_* operations for 2.6.33 — atomic per-CPU operations (this_cpu_read/write/add/etc) without explicit put_cpu() calls; simplifies per-CPU variable manipulation.
#HL 766#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367606/][Updegrove: FOSS introduction]]: Andy Updegrove's blog post introduction to free/open source software for newcomers — summarizes FOSS movement, ethical goals, contribution requirements; aimed at audiences unfamiliar with FOSS concepts.
#HL 767#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367630/][Writing an ACPI driver]]: Matthew Garrett's tutorial on writing ACPI drivers — uses Toshiba Bluetooth driver (TOS6205) example; covers DSDT table decompilation, ACPI device methods (_STA, BTST, AUSB, DUSB, BTPO, BTPF), acpi_evaluate_object(), notification handling, resume callbacks.
#HL 768#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367659/][Web Design for Developers]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book announcement by Brian Hogan — programmer's guide to design tools and techniques; covers Photoshop, CSS, web page redesign from concept to implementation.
#HL 769#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367660/][Security on Rails]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book by Ben Poweski and David Raphael — security techniques for Rails developers; risk assessment, authentication, authorization, cryptography, integrating external management systems.
#HL 770#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367787/][Two that didn't make it]]: Jonathan Corbet — Ceph distributed filesystem and AlacrityVM hypervisor not merged into 2.6.33; Linus says insufficient user advocacy; catches-22 between needing users to test vs distributions shipping out-of-tree code.
#HL 771#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367810/][pr_unwanted()?]]: Printk() macro discussion — Joe Perches converting printk to pr_* macros sparked debate; Peter Zijlstra reverted changes citing unnecessary complexity; pr_* macros for driver single-line messages still exist.
#HL 772#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367874/][Linux malware incident]]: Koen Vervloesem covers GNOME-Look.org malware (WaterFall screensaver) — .deb installed DDoS bot downloading scripts; lessons on user trust, package manager security, GPG-based web of trust proposals, mandatory VCS for KDE plugins.
#HL 773#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367878/][Moonlight covenant]]: Microsoft posted covenant not to sue for Moonlight 3/4 — narrow license only applies to Novell-implemented code; can be discontinued anytime; community debates usefulness.
#HL 774#new#new|- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/367895/][Turbulence for workqueues]]: Tejun Heo's concurrency-managed workqueues face scrutiny — Peter Zijlstra objects preferring threaded IRQs; complexity concerns; Ingo Molnar requests example conversions demonstrating advantages before 2.6.34 merge.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368747/][The SAY2K10 bug]]: SpamAssassin rule SAY2K10 incorrectly flagged emails with "2010" or later dates as spam when the year 2010 arrived — rule matched date patterns without proper year validation, causing legitimate emails to be marked as spam requiring immediate patch.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368861/][GSM encryption crack made public]]: Researchers demonstrated a practical attack on GSM's A5/1 encryption using 2 terabyte rainbow tables — enables interception of mobile calls with commodity hardware and open-source software (Airprobe), showing cellular encryption is weaker than assumed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368690/][The isolate utility]]: New program for running untrusted code in secure chroot-like environments with resource limits — provides per-process namespaces, CPU/memory constraints, and filesystem sandboxing for safely executing potentially malicious binaries.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368905/][list_sort()]]: Dave Chinner's new generic list_sort() function consolidated three different list sorting implementations — provides efficient O(n log n) sorting for kernel linked lists using a merge sort algorithm suitable for the existing list infrastructure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368730/][Restricting the network]]: Michael Stone's proposal for voluntary network access restrictions in Linux — discussed using the existing LSM (Linux Security Module) stacking infrastructure to allow processes to lock down their network capabilities.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368869/][Memory compaction]]: Mel Gorman's memory compaction patches to combat fragmentation — moves pages within NUMA nodes to create large contiguous blocks for high-order allocations, reducing allocation failures by reclaiming fragmented memory.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/368706/][RCU strings]]: Andi Kleen's RCU-based string type for safe concurrent sysctl string handling — uses read-copy-update synchronization to eliminate races between readers and writers when accessing string parameters, avoiding traditional locking overhead.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369549/][Timer slack]]: Arjan van de Ven's timer slack implementation allowing power-saving coalescing of timer events — programs can request timer slack to let the kernel group nearby timer expirations, reducing wake-ups and power consumption on idle systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369706/][The end of user-space mode setting?]]: Discussion of removing non-KMS (Kernel Mode Setting) support from Nouveau and Intel graphics drivers — distributions increasingly required KMS, making user-space mode setting obsolete and complicating driver maintenance.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369567/][sys_membarrier()]]: Mathieu Desnoyers' new system call for user-space RCU (Read-Copy-Update) implementations — provides a memory barrier across all running threads enabling userspace RCU implementations without kernel patches, with glibc integration proposed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369609/][FBAC-LSM]]: Functionality-Based Application Confinement (FBAC) Linux Security Module — implements hierarchical functionality permissions allowing administrators to define fine-grained access policies where processes can only use specific subsets of available system capabilities.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369511/][Speculating on page faults]]: Fix for page fault performance regression on 64-bit systems — rather than speculation being the problem, the issue was 64-bit rwsem implementation using inadequate atomic operations; fix involved using proper LL/SC instructions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369561/][Here We Go Again: The video standards war of 2010]]: Analysis of the HTML5 video codec battle (H.264 vs WebM/VP8) — discusses how DRM requirements and patent pools may force adoption of H.264 despite VP8 being open-source, echoing past format wars.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369399/][Wheeler: California says open source software is okay!]: California's declaration that free/open source software meets state procurement requirements — clarifies FLOSS is acceptable for government use, removing FUD around legal compliance for using open-source software in public sector.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/369099/][Red Hat CEO on recession, virtualization, and Ballmer]: Jim Whitehurst interview discussing Red Hat's strategy — covers how open-source model helped during recession, Red Hat's virtualization approach competing with VMware, and perspectives on Oracle/Sun acquisition implications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/370418/][devtmpfs to lose its EXPERIMENTAL tag]]: Kay Sievers' patch promoted devtmpfs from experimental to stable — devtmpfs creates device nodes at boot using kernel's driver model, reducing initramfs complexity and allowing device classes to populate /dev automatically.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/370419/][LCA: Why filesystems are hard]: Ted Ts'o Linux.conf.au talk on filesystem development challenges — filesystem quality requires years of testing, subtle bugs can cause data loss, and vendors face pressure to ship features before adequate validation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/370322/][Uprobes: not quite there yet]: dynamic user-space probing implementation status — uprobes allows placing breakpoints in user-space applications without stopping execution, similar to kprobes for kernel, but still had issues with multi-threaded applications and reliability.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/370423/][Secrets of the Ftrace function tracer]]: Steven Rostedt's detailed explanation of Ftrace internals — function tracer uses gcc's -pg profiling with mcount(), ring buffer for low-overhead event collection, and debugfs interface for controlling what functions are traced.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/370307/][0MQ: A new approach to messaging]: Introduction to 0MQ (ZeroMQ) messaging library — provides lightweight message queue patterns built on sockets, supports pub/sub, request/reply, and push/pull patterns with in-process, inter-process, and TCP transport, aiming to simplify network programming.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/371320/][A module for crashing the kernel]]: Simon Kagstrom's kernel module creates debugfs files (provoke_crash) for intentional kernel crashes — provides bugon, null_dereference, overwrite_allocation, corrupt_stack, oops_interrupt_context, write_after_free, unaligned_load_store for testing kmsg_dumper() and crash recovery; not expected for mainline due to opposition.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/371538/][fincore()]]: Chris Frost's proposed system call to check if file pages are in page cache — helps prefetch libraries decide how much data to prefetch without thrashing; application knows pages were evicted if fincore() shows them missing; Andrew Morton likes the "inner geek" appeal.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/371276/][LCA: Graphics driver ponies]]: Dave Airlie's linux.conf.au talk on kernel mode setting (KMS) state — Intel leads with feature-complete driver, ATI/Radeon in staging with R800 support coming, Nouveau merged for 2.6.33 KMS-only; TTM memory manager merged, Gallium 3D and Wayland on the horizon.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/371210/][Back to the drawing board for utrace?]]: Linus Torvalds rejected utrace over concerns about SystemTap depending on it — utrace provides no user-space interface, only hooks for kernel modules; called it "random crazy out-of-tree crap"; SystemTap may need to find alternative tracing solutions in ftrace/perf events.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/371501/][Replacing ptrace()]]: Discussion on why replacing ptrace() is hard — GDB needs to work on old kernels/platforms so thousands of lines of workaround code would remain; new Linux-only syscalls tend to see limited uptake; ptrace() will likely be maintained alongside any replacement for years.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/370985/][Blizzard: HTML5 video and H.264]]: Christopher Blizzard's blog post comparing H.264 licensing to the old GIF patent situation — warns that patent pools will increase royalties over time like they did with MP3; companies owning H.264 patents will charge more if it becomes fundamental web technology; argues for VP8/WebM as royalty-free alternative.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/372321/][The x86_64 DOS hole]]: CVE-2010-0307 kernel panic vulnerability on x86_64 — trying to exec() a 64-bit program from 32-bit mode then triggering core dump causes kernel panic due to corrupted personality setup; fix split flush_old_exec() and removed early SET_PERSONALITY() call.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/371986/][Lockdep-RCU]]: Paul McKenney's article on adding lockdep checking to RCU dereference primitives — new rcu_dereference_check() and related APIs let lockdep detect improper RCU usage; rcu_dereference() now warns if not in RCU read-side critical section; helps catch bugs in 350+ rcu_dereference() occurrences across kernel.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/372419/][Greg Kroah-Hartman: Android and the Linux kernel community]]: Greg KH blog on Android's kernel fork problem — Google created out-of-tree kernel infrastructure (wakelocks, binder, early suspend) that companies can't upstream; maintainers concerned about wakelocks being suboptimal compared to existing solutions; debate over whether fork was necessary vs. working with community.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/373405/][Who wrote 2.6.33]]: Statistics on 2.6.33 kernel development — 10,500 non-merge commits, 1,152 developers, 380,000 lines net growth; top contributors: Ben Hutchings/Frederic Weisbecker (145 changesets), Bartlomiej Zolnierkiewicz (206K lines changed); Red Hat leads employers, followed by Intel and IBM; 14.6% from independent developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/373842/][Scripting support for perf]]: Tom Zanussi added perl/python scripting to perf tool — embed interpreters in perf executable to process trace data; generate skeleton scripts with perf trace, edit to add functionality; example scripts for failed syscalls, wakeup latency, file I/O activity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/373550/][USB autosuspend]]: Oliver Neukum's article on USB runtime power management — usb_autopm_get/put_interface APIs for drivers to indicate when devices can suspend; remote wakeup support; autosuspend delay heuristic; ~7% power savings on laptops tested; drivers must avoid races in resume().
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/373656/][Counting users]]: Fedora's challenge counting users accurately — NAT undercounts unique IPs 2-4x; proposal to add UUID to yum queries for mirrorlist; privacy concerns about tracking vs opt-in; Debian popcon as alternative example; yum implemented $uuid variable.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/372929/][Language Implementation Patterns]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book by Terence Parr — teaches building DSLs and language parsers using 31 patterns; ANTLR-based; covers recognition, trees, interpretation, translation; makes language development practical for developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/373877/][Metaprogramming Ruby]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book by Paolo Perrotta — describes 34 "spells" for Ruby metaprogramming; covers object model, methods, blocks, class definitions; case study of metaprogramming in Rails; makes advanced Ruby techniques accessible.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/374776/][Compression formats for kernel.org]]: XZ format considered for kernel.org downloads — better compression (53MB vs 62MB bzip2) but tools not widely available; gzip will stay for compatibility; discussion about decompression speed vs compression ratio; parallel XZ decompression potential.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/374794/][Extended error reporting]]: Andi Kleen describes problem with errno-only error reporting — complex subsystems like V4L2 and networking return just EINVAL with no details; options discussed: printk, extending syscalls, or new errno-like mechanism with field pointers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/374633/][Merging kdb and kgdb]]: Jason Wessel proposed merging kdb into kgdb infrastructure — kdb shell underneath allows both source-level debugging (kgdb) and simple shell (kdb); supports arm, mips, powerpc, sparc; Ubuntu already enables kgdb in kernels.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/374574/][How old is our kernel?]]: Git blame analysis of kernel code age — ~31% still dates to 2.6.12 (2005); sound oldest subsystem (45%), tools newest (didn't exist pre-2.6.29); 1062 files untouched in 5 years; interesting discussion on "code half-life".
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/374424/][Huge pages part 1 (Introduction)]]: Mel Gorman's 5-part series introduction — huge pages improve TLB hit rates (2-45% performance gain for database/scientific workloads); libhugetlbfs utilities; NUMA considerations; reservation changes since kernel 2.6.29.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375888/][Open by handle]]: Aneesh Kumar's new syscalls name_to_handle() and open_by_handle() — enable user-space filesystem servers to generate file handles for backup/hsm; handles passed to clients for later file access; only privileged users can open by handle.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375976/][Reserved network ports]]: Octavian Purdila's ip_local_reserved_ports sysctl — allows admin to reserve ports so kernel won't allocate them for ephemeral sockets; solves NFS daemon port conflicts without libc hacks; going into 2.6.34.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375855/][A Checkpoint/restart update]]: 27K patch for container checkpoint/restart — checkpoint(pid, fd) and restart(pid, fd) syscalls; two-phase collect/serialize; supports screen/vnc sessions and live migration; security via ptrace checks and RESTART_KEEP_LSM flag.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375335/][2.6.32.9 Release notes]]: Jonathan Corbet analyzed 93 patches — 18 security-relevant; futex bugs (denial of service), NFS oopses, i915 fixes, USB audio oops, move_pages() infoleak (CVE-2010-0415); difficulty of identifying security implications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375096/][Huge pages part 2: Interfaces]]: Mel Gorman's interfaces guide — shmget() with SHM_HUGETLB, hugetlbfs filesystem, anonymous MAP_HUGETLB, libhugetlbfs APIs; stack cannot be backed by huge pages (no benefit with gcc).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375935/][Hg Init: a Mercurial tutorial]]: Joel Spolsky's extensive Mercurial tutorial — sparked Git vs Mercurial debate on ease of use, Windows support (TortoiseHg vs TortoiseGit), branching complexity for non-developers, CRLF handling; tutorial praised for humor and cross-platform applicability.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/375549/][A handbook for the open source way (opensource.com)]]: Opensource.com interview about "The Open Source Way" book project — aims to create canonical guide for applying open-source principles to business; chapter on "Business the open source way" seen as most exciting.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377101/][New features and configuration defaults]]: Jonathan Corbet covers kernel merge window issue — developers enabling CONFIG options by default (default y) for new features violates practice; Linus publicly rejected pulls for features defaulting y without config option or curing cancer.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377109/][Divorcing namespaces from processes]]: Eric Biederman's nsfd() and setns() syscalls — nsfd() returns fd referencing another process's namespace (requires ptrace capability); setns() lets process enter a namespace via fd; enables longer-lived namespaces independent of processes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377103/][Fishy business]]: Discussion about Android code names (mahimahi, trout, swordfish) being confusing — ARM maintainer Russell King decided to keep fishy names to avoid barriers to mainline; Android's multiple codenames through device lifecycle (Passion→Mahimahi→Nexus One) cause file naming inconsistencies.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/376508/][2.6.34 Merge window, part 1]]: Key changes: async suspend/resume merged (with on/off switch), perf lock command added, Python scripting in perf, vhost_net for efficient virtio networking, lockdep RCU patches, DECnet orphaned (no maintainer), IGMP snooping in bridge, many new drivers (Intel 82599, Atheros AR8151/8152 Ethernet, various audio/media/input chips).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/376606/][Huge pages part 3: Administration]]: Mel Gorman's huge page administration guide — identifying page sizes via sysfs or libhugetlbfs, static/dynamic huge page pool configuration via hugepages= kernel param or sysctl, hugetlbfs mounting with quotas, shmmax/shm_group tuning for shared memory, min_free_kbytes tuning to improve allocation success rates.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377060/][An introduction to the new development page]]: Announcement that long-time Development Page editor Forrest Cook departed; LWN thinning development page format due to resource constraints — major reader debate over loss of comprehensive software release coverage.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377063/][A look at Simple Scan]]: Joe Brockmeier's review of Simple Scan (Ubuntu Lucid's new GTK scanner app) — one-shot scanning, basic crop/rotate, PDF/JPEG/PNG export, email integration with Evolution, intended to replace complex XSane for basic tasks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378036/][QOTW 2: the zombie edition]]: Quote of the Week featuring Linus Torvalds rant about compress/mm.h ("nuke from orbit"), Peter Anvin EPA/zombie joke, Eric Paris on framework fragmentation — ongoing kernel API design discussions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377741/][LogFS merged into the mainline kernel]]: Jörn Engel's LogFS filesystem for raw flash (not SSD) merged in 2.6.34 — flash-aware design with wear leveling, journal, ECC; differs from NILFS2 (uses userspace daemon for GC); LogFS GC runs entirely in kernel for immediate space reuse.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378044/][A new deadline scheduler patch]]: SCHED_DEADLINE v2 by Dario Faggioli — deadline inheritance solves priority inversion (shortens deadline of resource holder); bandwidth throttling exemption during inheritance; still needs global multiprocessor support; ported to realtime preemption tree.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378043/][No huge pages article this week]]: Mel Gorman's huge pages series taking one-week intermission; fourth installment (benchmarking) coming next week.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377766/][2.6.34 Merge window, part 2]]: Key changes: synchronous signals delivered before async (fixes WINE context issue), new incompatible Nouveau driver (breaks Fedora 12 users), VGA switcheroo for hybrid graphics, LogFS merged, kprobes jump optimization, exofs RAID0 and groups support, early console open before root fs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377953/][Nouveau and interface compatibility]]: Linus Torvalds frustrated by Nouveau interface change breaking his Fedora 12 setup — Nouveau was merged at Linus's insistence as staging driver; debate on ABI stability in staging vs mainline; distributions shipping code before upstream creates tester problems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/377895/][4K-sector drives and Linux]]: Linux block layer handles 4K physical sectors well; complications from BIOS, partitioners (fdisk uses CHS legacy), XP compatibility (drives implement 512B logical/4K physical); alignment issues with sector 63; WD drives with off-by-one "Aligned Partitioning" hack; tools like libblkid, parted updated.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378911/][Big reader locks]]: Nick Piggin's brlock (big reader lock) for VFS scalability — per-CPU spinlocks for read access (no cache bouncing), writers acquire all NR_CPUS locks; good for read-mostly data like vfsmount_lock used in pathname lookups.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378859/][Who let the hogs out?]]: Tejun Heo's cpuhog mechanism monopolizes CPUs for kernel operations — used by stop_machine(), migration threads, scheduler transitions; cleaned up migration thread, improved boot performance; hog functions cannot sleep.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378641/][Huge pages part 4: benchmarking with huge pages]]: Mel Gorman's benchmark results: STREAM 11-16% improvement, Sysbench OLTP 1-3.5%, SpecCPU int 13%, floating-point 7-8%, SpecJVM 4.4% average; libhugetlbfs tools (hugeadm, hugectl) simplify configuration.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/378884/][A critical look at sysfs attribute values]]: Neil Brown's analysis — "one item per file" rule inconsistently enforced; inconsistent units (bytes/kb/sectors, ms/us/s); no standard for enumerated types; structured data needs not addressed; proposes standardized attribute types (duration, temperature, storage-size) and deprecation mechanism.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/380170/][SSL on kernel.org]]: John "Warthog9" Hawley announced SSL encryption for kernel.org — bugzilla, wikis, account requests, and Patchwork now default to https; www, boot, git, and android.git subdomains support SSL if user specifies https; no plans for mirrors.kernel.org due to memory/scale constraints; Thawte donated wildcard SSL certificates.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/380141/][Piecemeal tracepoints?]]: Jan Kara proposed selectively enabling tracepoints per subsystem at build time — concern was tracepoint checks pollute non-targeted kernel paths; kernel hackers rejected idea citing minimal overhead from jump label optimization and value of having all tracepoints built-in for debugging; Thomas Gleixner noted tracepoints "are an all or nothing proposition."
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/380150/][The end for Video4Linux1]]: Hans Verkuil's multi-stage plan to remove V4L1 from kernel — Phase 1 converts remaining V4L1 drivers to V4L2; Phase 2 removes V4L1 compatibility layer (allows old apps to work with V4L2 drivers) pushing support to userspace libv4l1 library; compatibility break may affect xawtv users; removal planned for 2.6.36.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/379869/][KVM, QEMU, and kernel project management]]: Flame war between Ingo Molnar and KVM/QEMU developers over "perf kvm" — Inyo proposed host mounting guest filesystems read-only and guest enumeration for easier profiling; Avi Kivity and KVM team rejected citing security concerns and project management philosophy; Ingo's suggestion to merge QEMU into kernel tree was strongly opposed; "perf kvm" feature essentially scrapped.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/379903/][Using the TRACE_EVENT() macro (Part 1)]]: Steven Rostedt's tutorial on kernel tracepoints — TRACE_EVENT() macro automates tracepoint creation with six components: name, prototype, args, struct, assign, print; enables developers to add tracepoints without understanding Ftrace internals; tracepoints are agnostic to tracers (used by Ftrace, perf, LTTng, SystemTap); requires following header file format in include/trace/events/.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/379748/][Huge pages part 5: A deeper look at TLBs and costs]]: Mel Gorman's final installment on huge pages — covers TLB structure and measurement using oprofile and Calibrator tool; estimates TLB miss latency (7-19 cycles on X86, ~563 cycles on PPC64); demonstrates 12-17% performance improvement from huge pages using STREAM benchmark; includes tlbmiss_cost.sh script in libhugetlbfs for measuring TLB costs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/381158/][Toward a saner execve()]]: Andy Lutomirski's PR_RESTRICT_ME prctl() proposal — allows processes to disable execve() for security; adds execve_nosecurity() syscall that performs no security transitions; criticized as "awful naming" and potential "masturbation by API" unlikely to be used; addresses concerns about privilege restriction without setuid complications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/381164/][The BKL end game]]: Arnd Bergmann's patch series to eliminate Big Kernel Lock — replaces BKL in block and tty subsystems with mutexes; audits ioctl/llseek functions; explicitly marks remaining BKL-dependent code in kernel config; 148 modules still use BKL (including USB); major step toward BKL-free kernels.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/380931/][Disabling IRQF_DISABLED]]: Thomas Gleixner/Ingo Molnar proposal to run all interrupt handlers with interrupts disabled — IRQF_DISABLED flag becomes no-op in 2.6.35; slow handlers moved to threaded handlers; eliminates fast/slow handler distinction; addresses nested interrupt stack overflow issues; embedded systems concerns addressed via local_irq_enable_in_hardirq().
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/380835/][Evolutionary development of a semantic patch using Coccinelle]]: Wolfram Sang's tutorial on Coccinelle semantic patching — uses i2c driver clientdata clearing as example; creates semantic patch to find dangling pointers before kfree(); matched 96 drivers in 23 directories changing 213 lines; tool understands C syntax unlike sed/perl scripts; allows incremental patch development with alternations for different code patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/381064/][Using the TRACE_EVENT() macro (Part 2)]]: Steven Rostedt's continuation on tracepoints — DECLARE_EVENT_CLASS() and DEFINE_EVENT() macros reduce footprint by sharing functions across similar events (XFS text reduced 36% using class); covers __string, __dynamic_array macros for variable-length data; TP_printk helpers __print_flags and __print_symbolic for symbolic output; live demo enabling module and irq trace events.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/382554/][A "live mode" for perf]: Tom Zanussi's perf live mode allowing record/report via pipe — no need for separate record then analyze steps; activated when output goes to stdout or input from stdin; enables top-style continuously updating perf trace; perf becomes "swiss army knife" of kernel monitoring.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/382559/][The NO_BOOTMEM patches]: Yinghai Lu's CONFIG_NO_BOOTMEM to eliminate bootmem allocator — extends early_res mechanism to bootstrap buddy allocator directly; merged in 2.6.34 but caused regressions after -rc3 leading to Linus threatening revert; worst problems fixed; future plans include replacing early_res with logical memory block allocator.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/382299/][Memory management for virtualization]]: Discussion of transparent huge pages for guests — Andrea Arcangeli's patches allow huge pages without app awareness; Linus dismissed as "get a better CPU" issue but feature may still go in; VMware balloon driver patches for dynamic guest memory control; Dan Magenheimer's transcendent memory proposal for cooperative memory sharing between VMs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/382428/][Receive flow steering]]: Tom Herbert's RFS enhancement to RPS (Receive Packet Steering) — tracks CPU where application runs and steers packets there; uses two hash tables (rps_sock_flow_table for desired CPU, rps_dev_flow_table for current CPU); avoids out-of-order packets by checking backlog queue state; Google production-tested; 2.9x improvement in netperf transactions/sec.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/382257/][The padata parallel execution mechanism]]: Jonathan Corbet explains padata — kernel mechanism for parallel task execution with ordering preserved; developed for IPsec crypto but general enough for other uses; API includes padata_alloc/start/stop, padata_do_parallel/serial; parallel() callback does work, serial() called after completion on designated CPU; crypto/pcrypt.c uses it.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/381667/][The role of the Debian ftpmasters]]: Joe Brockmeier's profile of Debian's ftpmaster team — maintains archive, processes NEW packages, runs scripts for incoming packages; only 2 masters (Jaspert, Mark Hymers) plus 6 assistants; training period 6 months for assistants, 6 months minimum before upgrading to master; decides what goes into Debian archive; rejected qmail for policy/FHS violations; deals with legal/licensing issues.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/383368/][Idle cycle injection]]: Salman Qazi's kidled patches from Google — forces CPU idle cycles to prevent overheating/power spikes; controlled via /proc/sys/kernel/kidled; allows setting idle percentage per CPU; cgroup-based "interactive" process marking avoids impeding interactive workloads; "power capping priority" charges idle time to specific processes; addresses datacenter power infrastructure constraints rather than CPU overheating.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/383162/][The case of the overly anonymous anon_vma]]: Rik van Riel's anon_vma restructuring to fix O(N) scanning — original design put all COWed pages under one anon_vma causing "catastrophic failure" with 1000 processes; new anon_vma_chain structure links per-process anon_vmas; fixes null pointer oops after hibernation where child's anon_vma disappeared; Linus debugged by examining register values in oops output; 2.6.34-rc4 delayed 2 weeks to fix.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384092/][Ceph: The Distributed File System Creature from the Object Lagoon (Linux Mag)]]: Linux Magazine feature on Ceph filesystem merged in 2.6.34 — designed for large-scale dynamic storage with hardware failures; presumptuous assumption that storage systems are dynamic and failures inevitable; provides resilient distributed filesystem.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384132/][Fixing the ondemand governor]]: Arjan van de Ven's fix changes cpufreq ondemand governor to ignore I/O wait time in idle calculation — prevents CPU frequency dropping during CPU+I/O alternating workloads like git grep; original conservative governor had similar issues but with slower ramp up; Arjan planning complete rewrite of ondemand governor for fundamental fixes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384139/][DM and MD come a little closer]]: Neil Brown's dm-raid456 module builds RAID implementation for device mapper on MD code — aims to eliminate duplicated RAID code between MD and DM subsystems; brings RAID6 support and multiple-target support to device mapper; early work but positive response from DM maintainers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384118/][ELC: Using LTTng]]: Mathieu Desnoyers' Embedded Linux Conference tutorial on LTTng tracing — covers lockless trace clock, tracing strategies (producer-consumer vs flight recorder modes), channels for grouping events, anchors/triggers for analysis, live demo diagnosing X.org audio latency; discusses LTTng status for mainline inclusion with Ftrace developer Rostedt agreeing on collaboration.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384093/][When writeback goes wrong]]: Dave Chinner's patch disables writeback in direct reclaim to fix stack overflow — deep call chains through complex storage (union mount + RAID + iSCSI) exhaust 8K kernel stacks; skipping writeback in direct reclaim avoids stack pressure but may increase OOM frequency; lumpy reclaim creates seeky I/O patterns; Andrew Morton says problem is 2.6.16 regression in page reclaim behavior.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/383362/][Using the TRACE_EVENT() macro (Part 3)]]: Steven Rostedt's guide to adding tracepoints in kernel modules — covers defining trace headers outside include/trace/events, TRACE_INCLUDE_PATH for module-specific headers, CREATE_TRACE_POINTS macro usage, Makefile CFLAGS setup for local includes; explains cpp tricks behind TRACE_EVENT() macro; demonstrates combining events with function graph tracer for interrupt latency analysis; 2.6.34-rc3 has 341 TRACE_EVENT() macros.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384936/][CPUS*PIDS = mess]]: Mike Travis discovered 2048-processor systems hit PID limit (32K) with only 16 processes per CPU — kernel threads alone can exhaust PIDs; proposed solutions included boot parameters for larger PID space but rejected as temporary; likely will use heuristics to auto-adjust limits based on CPU count; concern about 16-bit signed int apps still running on big systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/385103/][Suspend block]]: Arve Hjønnevåg's suspend block patches replace Android's wakelock API for mainline — introduces /sys/power/policy with "opportunistic" mode allowing automatic suspend when idle; suspend_blocker API at kernel/user-space levels prevents unwanted suspension; patches getting acked, likely for 2.6.35 merge; should enable Android driver code merging.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/385081/][Kernel Hacker's Bookshelf: Generating Realistic Impressions for File-System Benchmarking]]: Valerie Aurora's review of Impressions tool by Agrawal et al — creates realistic reproducible file system images for benchmarking using statistical models; handles directory depth, file sizes (log-normal + Pareto distribution), fragmentation; open-source (GPLv3), needs maintainer; addresses longstanding fs benchmarking flaws (Andrew benchmark from 1988, Postmark's lack of fsync).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384855/][Might 2.6.35 be BKL-free?]]: Discussion of removing big kernel lock from Linux — locked_ioctl() approach rejected by Linus; alternatives proposed: rename all ioctl() to bkl_ioctl() for easy grep, or push BKL down into individual drivers; CONFIG_BKL to make BKL optional; scheduler context switch overhead eliminated when BKL unused; TTY layer remains problematic.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384146/][The cpuidle subsystem]]: Jonathan Corbet's deep dive into cpuidle for CPU power management — explains C-states (C1/C2/C3) with exit latency and power consumption; cpuidle driver layer abstracts hardware differences; governors implement policy for selecting idle states based on latency requirements and pm_qos; enter() function handles state transitions; sysfs exposes state data at /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpuN/cpuidle.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/384713/][Tools and distributions for embedded Linux development]]: Tom Parkin's comprehensive survey of embedded Linux ecosystem — covers DIY (Cross Linux From Scratch), build frameworks (Buildroot, OpenEmbedded/Bitbake, Scratchbox, Firmware Linux), slimmed desktop distros (Emdebian, Gentoo Embedded), commercial offerings (MontaVista, Wind River), and complete stacks (Android, Maemo/MeeGo); notes shift toward native builds on capable ARM hardware.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/386330/][A rough restart for checkpoints]]: Checkpoint/restart 100-patch series not getting reviewed attention — developers posted before 2.6.35 merge window; overwhelmed reviewers intimidated by patch size; likely delayed until after merge window; would benefit long-running scientific jobs and embedded devices with limited memory.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/386331/][De-bloating tracepoints]]: Steven Rostedt's patch reduces tracepoint overhead 100KB — moves information to shared locations; DEFINE_EVENT reduced from 700 to 250 bytes; 616 syscalls plus 82 events gave 103KB savings; makes enabling tracepoints in production kernels more practical.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/386090/][Cleancache and Frontswap]]: Dan Magenheimer's transcendent memory abstractions for virtualization — Cleancache is victim cache for clean pages (recoverable from disk); Frontswap handles dirty pages with guaranteed retrieval; enables compression (ramzswap/CompCache), deduplication, SSD caching; already in OpenSUSE 11.2, Oracle VM, Xen.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/386139/][Reworking pm_qos]]: Mark Gross's API rework removes string-based requirement identification — new API uses opaque pm_qos_request_list handles; eliminates list walking and string comparisons for faster latency-sensitive operations; CPU/network latency and throughput parameters; should merge in 2.6.35.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/385988/][An In-Depth Look at Gentoo Linux (Kernel News)]]: Kernel News review of Gentoo Linux — focuses on Portage package manager; compiles from source allowing custom USE flags; reviewer praises choice and flexibility; Gentoo avoids release upgrade cycles; can run ~arch (unstable) packages; 40 systems upgraded over years without reinstall.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/385376/][Can't Program, won't Program? Then Mash the Web with Mozilla's Ubiquity]]: Free Software Magazine's look at Mozilla Ubiquity — natural language command interface for browser; described as "social command line" and "Web 3.0 mashup"; aims to let non-programmers interact with web APIs through conversational commands.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443099/][Seccomp: replacing security modules?]]: Ingo Molnar suggests expanding seccomp to replace LSM — proposes hooking into perf events for arbitrary kernel event filtering; would let unprivileged apps set security policies; James Morris says real security should be at LSM level; Eric Paris notes apps can't rely on LSM presence; future may hold event-based filters.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443379/][Pushback on pointer hiding]]: Developer resistance to hiding kernel addresses by default in 2.6.39 — /proc/kallsyms zeroed addresses broke perf; David Miller noted SELinux isn't on by default; final decision: kptr_restrict=0 default, users who want security can set it; pointer hiding only useful with kernel address randomization.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443241/][Integrating memory control groups]]: Johannes Weiner's memcg naturalization patches — eliminates duplicated LRU lists by making per-group LRU the only LRU; root group holds uncharged pages; reclaim now traverses control group hierarchy; improves fairness across groups; shrinks code by 400+ lines; eliminates 16MB overhead for page_cgroup structures on 4GB system.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443510/][ARM kernel consolidation]]: Paul McKenney on Linaro effort to consolidate ARM architecture code — organizes ARM code by function not SoC/board; drivers move to proper subsystems; struct clk, device tree, generic interrupt chip already shared across architectures; new git tree with Arnd Bergmann, Nicolas Pitre, Marc Zyngier as maintainers; targets 2.6.41 merge window.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443531/][The platform problem]]: Jonathan Corbet's essay on treating kernel platform as immutable — recounts reinvention of videobuf functionality in cafe_ccic driver; encourages developers to fix common code rather than work around; ARM kernel has severe case of platform problem; separate repositories not the real issue.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443279/][UDS security discussions]]: Jake Edge's coverage of Ubuntu Developer Summit security track — community involvement in universe package updates; security team handles signing process; USNs no longer posted to Bugtraq; format standardization for security notices; whitepaper on vulnerability statistics considered.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442657/][Distribution quotes of the week]]: Notable quotes — documentation importance (yum remove gnome* scenario), CentOS6 delay after RHEL6 release (Greg Smith on CentOS decline).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443385/][LTTng in the Ubuntu kernel]]: Julien Desfossez proposing LTTng for Ubuntu 11.10/12.04 — 2.0-distro version requires minimal kernel changes; modularized ring buffer; Mathieu Desnoyers later found way to need no core changes; PPA for 11.10, aim for 12.04 LTS inclusion.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442576/][What Every C Programmer Should Know About Undefined Behavior #1/3]]: LLVM blog series on C undefined behavior — signed integer overflow is undefined (compiler can eliminate checks); uninitialized variables; type aliasing with restrict; sequence points; examples from Doom's P_Random() demonstrating unspecified evaluation order.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443037/][What every C Programmer should know about undefined behavior #2/3]]: Second installment — tools for finding bugs (sparse, Polyspace, Klee); compiler optimization of NULL checks after use; initializing before NULL check causes problems; discussion on C vs C++ private keyword; Java reflection accessing private members.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/443604/][Poettering: systemd for developers I]]: Lennart Poettering's new series on systemd for developers — socket activation example showing shorter code; service works with and without socket activation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442268/][A brief experiment with PyPy]]: Jonathan Corbet's PyPy experiment — gitdm ran 3x faster on PyPy (21s vs 63s); CPython had fewer cache misses but more syscalls; PyPy's JIT works well for pure Python; extension modules still a barrier.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441790/][Scale Fail (part 1)]]: Josh Berkus on application scaling anti-patterns — trendiness (choosing tech for prestige not fit), no metrics, barn door decisions, single-threaded programming; single-threaded not actually the enemy; SPoFs and caching covered in part 2.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442042/][AMD and Coreboot]]: AMD announced Coreboot support for future processors including Llano APU — opened AGESA bridge code for coreboot integration; significant for HPC and cloud deployments; allows customizing boot firmware without proprietary BIOS.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442113/][Ftrace, perf, and the tracing ABI]]: powertop broke when lock_depth field removed from tracepoints — tracepoints are ABI; applications should read format files but many hardcode offsets; perf vs ftrace tension; Google cares about event size.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442355/][Stable pages]]: Darrick Wong's patch to make pages under writeback wait for writes — prevents data corruption with integrity-checked hardware; 12% performance hit possible; ext3 may not support due to journal complications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/442334/][Introduction to programming in Erlang (developerWorks)]]: IBM developerWorks introduction to Erlang — concurrency model, fault tolerance, distributed processing; functional paradigm different from imperative languages; linked to devworks series.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441377/][The Open Wireless Movement kernel wiki]]: Luis Rodriguez created wiki for open wireless network safety — EFF's open wireless movement; kernel developers gathering info on securing open APs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441207/][Interview with Linus Torvalds (LinuxFR)]]: LinuxFR interview covering Android fork, ethics of licenses, DRM — Linus sees forks as healthy; doesn't push particular license ethics; git embodies the fork-and-merge workflow; discussion on hardware rights vs software freedom.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441438/][Mob rule for dentries]]: Pavel Emelyanov's per-container dentry cache management patches — organizes dentries into "mobs" by filesystem subtree; allows limiting dentry cache per container; three new ioctl calls (FIMOBROOT, FIMOBSIZE, FIMOBSTAT).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441209/][Raw events and the perf ABI]]: Offcore events removed from perf because interface was too low-level — Ingo wants generalized events instead of raw hex codes; users can still get raw events but should use higher-level interface; concerns about ABI stability.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441232/][Expanding seccomp]]: Will Drewry's seccomp filter expansion using Ftrace infrastructure — allows filtering syscalls by arguments; prctl interface with filter expressions; would help Chromium sandbox; useful for containers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/441018/][LFCS: Building the kernel with Clang]]: LLVM Linux project building kernel with Clang — 90%+ drivers compile; Broadcom wireless and NVIDIA work; issues with VLAIS, -fno-optimize-sibling-calls, -mregparm; boot code requires GAS not IA.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/440246/][ABS: The guts of Android]]: Karim Yaghmour's Android Builders Summit talk on Android internals — covers Android's non-standard Linux kernel (wakelocks, Binder), its Java-based user space with Dalvik VM, custom Bionic libc, and startup sequence (bootloader → init → Zygote → System Service → ActivityManager); uses intents for IPC, ext4 on newer devices; GPL concerns led to D-Bus for BlueZ.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/440347/][Dcache scalability and security modules]]: Fix for 2.6.38 dcache scalability issue where security modules forced fallback to slow pathname lookup — Andi Kleen's patches made SELinux and SMACK RCU-safe for inode_permission checks; systems with security modules enabled now get fastpath benefits; auditing still causes slowdowns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/440255/][The return of SEEK_HOLE]]: Josef Bacik re-proposed SEEK_HOLE/SEEK_DATA lseek() options for finding file holes — FIEMAP ioctl proved too complex and error-prone for simple apps like cp; SEEK_HOLE provides simpler interface for sparse file detection used by backup utilities; compatible with Solaris implementation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/440221/][ARM, DMA, and memory management]]: ARM IOMMU and DMA API challenges on ARM architecture — conflicting memory mapping attributes problem, CMA allocator for contiguous DMA buffers, graphics drivers need uncached write-combining buffers for GPU texture handling; future need for buffer sharing between devices via generalized GEM memory manager.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/440064/][ELC: A PREEMPT_RT roadmap]]: Thomas Gleixner's realtime Linux roadmap at Embedded Linux Conference — remaining pieces: preemptible mmu_gather, per-CPU data structure annotations, preemptible page allocators, threaded softirqs, sleeping spinlocks; ~20 active contributors; mainline merge "by end of next year" with small incremental Trojan horse patches.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/440279/][The Amnesic Incognito Live System: A live CD for anonymity]]: Tails privacy-focused live Linux distribution — built on Debian Squeeze, forces all traffic through Tor network, leaves no local traces, includes memory wiping on shutdown, HTTPS Everywhere, browser fingerprint protection; used for activism and journalism.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439337/][ABS: Android beyond the phone]]: Marko Gargenta's Marakana keynote on Android uses beyond phones — printers, DoD devices, Cisco Cius enterprise tablet, set-top boxes, networked cars; Android's app framework and complete stack appeal to device makers; concerns about Honeycomb source availability and enterprise security/management.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438478/][TI introduces OpenLink]]: Texas Instruments announced open-source WiFi/Bluetooth/FM connectivity drivers for ARM platforms — merged into vanilla kernel 2.6.39, supports BeagleBoard/PandaBoard, works with Android/MeeGo; no out-of-tree patches needed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438577/][MIPS Technologies Launches New Developer Community]]: MIPS launched developer.mips.com community site — targets Android on MIPS, provides Linux kernel source, NDK, development tools, forums; aims to compete with ARM in mobile/embedded space.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439472/][DISCONTIGMEM, !NUMA, and SLUB]]: Bug where DISCONTIGMEM causes SLUB allocator crashes on non-NUMA systems — DISCONTIGMEM maps memory regions to fake NUMA nodes confusing SLUB; discussion on fixing without breaking embedded systems; problem involves complex tradeoffs between memory models and allocator assumptions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439314/][Rationalizing the ARM tree]]: Russell King and Linus Torvalds criticized ARM architecture code growth — 75% of arch-specific changes in linux-next are ARM, ~6000 new lines; Linus threatened to not pull ARM tree unless cleanup happens; solution is to consolidate duplicated drivers (GPIO, interrupt chips, clocksource) and use Device Tree to reduce mach/* directories.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439419/][Managing source code with Mercurial (developerWorks)]]: IBM developerWorks introduction to Mercurial DVCS — triggered debate on Mercurial vs Git; Mercurial has simpler default commands but requires extensions for advanced features; Git has local branches and more powerful rebasing; discussion on branch semantics differences between the two systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437929/][LFCS: Linux penetration, Yocto, and hardware success stories]]: Jim Zemlin's Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit keynote — 95% of top500 supercomputers run Linux, 72% equity trading; Yocto 1.0 released for embedded distro building; hardware panel with TI/Qualcomm/Intel on upstreaming drivers; embedded Linux talent acquisition increasing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438182/][The native KVM tool]]: Pekka Enberg's lightweight KVM management tool as QEMU alternative — minimal features (serial console, no graphics/networking/SMP), clean compact code, easier debugging; being extended with virtio networking and SMP support.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437981/][A JIT for packet filters]]: Eric Dumazet's BPF JIT compiler for 64-bit x86 — translates BPF bytecode to native x86 instructions, 50ns savings per filter invocation; BPF is used by tcpdump and socket filters; potential future application to nftables for firewall rule JIT compilation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438256/][Explicit block device plugging]]: Jens Axboe's 2.6.39 kernel rewrite of block device plugging — replaced per-device state with per-task blk_plug structure allowing multiple related I/O requests to be batched before dispatch, reducing lock contention and improving request merging for better disk throughput.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438155/][LFCS: ARM, control groups, and the next 20 years]]: Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit kernel panel covering ARM community fragmentation (500+ SoCs, 70 sub-architectures), control groups code quality concerns, Linaro collaboration efforts, and speculation on Linux in 2031 — Gleixner predicted PREEMPT_RT merge before retirement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437602/][systemd for Administrators, Part VI]]: Lennart Poettering's systemd series part 6 — explains chroot() environment handling in systemd where daemons run in clean, independent contexts without inheriting user shell environment variables unlike sysvinit-based systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438169/][Poettering: systemd for Administrators, Part VII]]: systemd-analyze blame and plot tools for boot time analysis — emphasizes filing bugs at the right subsystem rather than just blaming slow boot services.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437142/][Kernel release status]]: 2.6.39-rc2 status and stable kernel updates — Linus noted uncommonly calm -rc2 release, suspicious of quiet development period.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/436871/][Linux Filesystem, Storage, and Memory Management Summit, Day 1]]: 2011 summit coverage — writeback problems and direct reclaim elimination discussed (Jan Kara's simpler patch vs Fengguang's bandwidth-based approach), VFS scalability patches status, transcendent memory/zcache updates, memory control group usage by Google/Fujitsu/Red Hat/Parallels/Taobao, memory compaction status, NVM Express standard introduction.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437066/][Linux Filesystem, Storage, and Memory Management Summit, Day 2]]: Second day coverage — I/O bandwidth controllers (throttling vs proportional), working set estimation for job placement, VM memory sizing with balloon drivers and page hinting, dirty limits in control groups, transparent huge page improvements, NUMA home node proposal, stable pages for writes-in-flight, 9p filesystem improvements for virtualization.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/436041/][Jump label reworked]]: Jump label API rework for 2.6.40 — simplified interface using struct jump_label_key with jump_label_inc/dec and static_branch; enables runtime toggle of unlikely code paths with minimal overhead when jump label support is configured.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/436047/][Powering down APM]]: Len Brown's proposal to remove APM power management support in 2.6.40 — APM obsolete since 2006 (no hardware or Windows support), but removal concerns raised for legacy systems; possibly keep power-off functionality while removing idle support.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435894/][Dynamic devices and static configuration]]: PandaBoard USB-Ethernet interface naming (usb0 vs eth0) and MAC address problems — discussion of platform_data expansion vs device tree approach for non-discoverable embedded hardware; short-term patches provided while longer-term solutions debated.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435917/][Fighting fork bombs]]: Hiroyuki Kamezawa's fork bomb tracking and killing mechanism — adds persistent process tree tracking to identify entire process families even after parent exit, detects fork bombs via memory allocation stalls, depth-first traversal to find and kill all descendants of high-memory processes when OOM fires.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434763/][Report from the V4L2 Warsaw Brainstorming Meeting]]: Three-day brainstorming session covering compressed video format APIs for MPEG/H.264, subdev hierarchy and pool improvements, cropping/composing ioctls, HDMI/CEC rework, buffer pool infrastructure for Linaro, multiple buffer queues, sensor/flash/snapshot functionality.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435022/][Converting strings to integers]]: New kstrto*() functions for 2.6.39 — standardized string-to-integer converters (kstrtoull, kstrtol, kstrtoint, etc.) marked __must_check to replace old problematic functions like simple_strtoul().
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434833/][The dynamic debugging interface]]: dynamic_debug kernel feature explanation — pr_debug()/dev_dbg() calls controlled via /sys/kernel/debug/dynamic_debug/control using selectors (file, function, module, format) and flags (+p, -p, f/l/m/t) for runtime debug output control.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434821/][Persistent storage for a kernel's "dying breath"]]: Tony Luck and Thomas Gleixner's pstore filesystem for 2.6.39 — generic framework for saving crash information to platform-specific persistent storage (ACPI ERST, flash, etc.) across reboots, mounted at /dev/pstore.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434901/][R Cookbook]]: O'Reilly cookbook by Paul Teetor for R statistical programming — 200+ recipes covering data structures, statistics, graphics, linear regression, practical data analysis.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435064/][O'Reilly Media and Fluidinfo Contest]]: O'Reilly and Fluidinfo API contest for developers to create applications using O'Reilly book metadata in Fluidinfo's writable API.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433787/][Diving into the Linux Networking Stack, Part I]]: Michael Schultz's tutorial on Linux networking stack — driver initialization and packet reception flow through igb driver example.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433904/][A group scheduling demonstration]]: Jonathan Corbet's demonstration of per-session group scheduling in 2.6.38 — runaway GUI processes isolated to their own cgroup, desktop remained responsive despite heavy load.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433568/][Uprobes: 11th time is the charm?]]: Uprobes dynamic user-space probing update — execute-out-of-line mechanism for breakpoint insertion, ftrace integration, SystemTap interest but gdb suitability questioned; controversial XOL VMA injection approach.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433601/][APIs for sensors]]: Sensor subsystem API discussion — pressure sensor driver rejected from input subsystem (not human input), IIO subsystem for analog-to-digital converters, debate over hwmon vs miscdevice vs IIO location.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433107/][Kuhn: GPL Compliance of Red Hat Linux Distribution]]: Bradley Kuhn's analysis of RHEL GPL compliance — Red Hat's changelog in src.rpm satisfies letter of GPLv2§2(a) but criticized for obfuscating kernel changes; community debate on "preferred form for modifications".
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433561/][Qt and Digia, facts and fiction]]: Qt Blog clarification after Nokia-Digia deal — 400K developers, 3500 commercial customers, Nokia continues investing in Qt, LGPL licensing maintained, KDE Free Qt Foundation guarantees BSD-style license if FLOSS releases cease.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/432871/][HP: The Linux Desktop Company]]: ZDNet coverage of HP shipping WebOS devices — HP's strategy to avoid Windows license costs, WebOS on tablets/notebooks/printers/phones, discussion of Linux desktop adoption.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433637/][LPI Hosts Exam Labs in Poland and Greece]]: Linux Professional Institute certification exam labs at 4Developers conference in Warsaw and Thessaloniki.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/427048/][Linus Torvalds interview]]: ITWire interview covering Linux evolution, mobile phones (Nokia mentioned), community growth vs early hacker days, technical challenge remains fun.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/427104/][Increasing the TCP initial congestion window]]: Google's patch to increase TCP initial congestion window from 4 to 10 segments — 10% latency reduction in tests, also raises initial receive window to 10 segments in 2.6.38.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426961/][Removing ext2 and/or ext3]]: Jan Kara's proposal to drop ext2/ext3 codebase — ext4 can mount ext2/3 with compatibility and optimizations like delayed allocation, but compatibility modes less tested; concerns about ext2 bitrot and testing gaps for non-native ext4 modes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426921/][Supporting multiple LSMs]]: David Howells' multi-LSM stacking framework patches — allows multiple security modules to register and be called for access decisions; Glass LSM alternative from Casey Schaufler uses different composition approach; secid handling problematic for SELinux+Smack combination.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426947/][Mesh networking with batman-adv]]: BATMAN-adv mesh networking merged into 2.6.38 — works at link layer via virtual network device, broadcasts originator messages for routing discovery, scales to ~1000 nodes; limited security against spoofed OGMs; useful for building/neighborhood connectivity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426912/][FOSDEM: Collaboration between distributions]]: FOSDEM 2011 distribution track — Debian/Fedora/openSUSE collaboration manifesto, downstream packaging cooperation, Mageia fork from Mandriva, Gentoo governance reform.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426451/][Distribution quotes of the week]]: Linux community quotes — Debian on BeagleBoards, Joe Brockmeier on openSUSE release schedules.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478627/][Format string vulnerabilities]]: Jake Edge's detailed explanation of format string vulnerabilities using the sudo bug as example — user-controlled argv[0] passed as format string to vfprintf(), allowing privilege escalation via %n format specifier to overwrite UID; fix is using %s in final print statement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478139/][Format string vulnerability in sudo]]: Brief note that sudo 1.8.0-1.8.3p1 has a format string vulnerability in sudo_debug() that can crash or potentially escalate privileges; fixed in 1.8.3p2; -D_FORTIFY_SOURCE=2 helps block exploits.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478635/][KaKaRoTo: How the ECDSA algorithm works]]: Youness Alaoui explains elliptic curve digital signature algorithm math — Sony's PS3 used weak ECDSA implementation with predictable random numbers, allowing private key extraction; fixed in firmware 3.56 with new keys.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478440/][What happened to disk performance in 2.6.39]]: Jonathan Corbet investigates SSD performance drop in 2.6.39 — explicit plugging/unplugging in generic_file_aio_read() caused readahead I/O to stall; fix removes top-level plugging so readahead requests bypass the plug and reach hardware immediately.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478111/][Preparing for user-space checkpoint/restore]]: Covers CRIU (kernel patches for process checkpoint/restore via prctl, /proc extensions, kcmp() syscall) and DMTCP (pure user-space solution using LD_PRELOAD wrappers, supports MPI, no kernel changes needed).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496418/][Who owns your data?]]: Jake Edge discusses digital heritage and data preservation — argues open formats trump proprietary/DRM-locked formats; free software supports old formats longer than vendors; Internet Archive can only preserve so much; users should demand open standards from businesses and governments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496583/][TizenConf: Pitching HTML5 as a development framework]]: Nathan Willis covers Tizen Developer Conference — HTML5/Web API as primary dev platform, Smack-based security, ConnMan 1.0 with fast DHCP, W3C Core Mobile Web Platform Group participation, Facebook's RingMark compliance test tool; small community but "code leads" strategy.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496158/][Accounting systems: a rant and a quest]]: Jonathan Corbet recounts LWN's QuickBooks hitting hidden 14,500 item limit forcing $2400 enterprise upgrade — impetus to finally migrate to free software accounting; surveys landscape: GnuCash/KMyMoney too basic, enterprise tools too complex; ledger-style plain-text approach discussed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496099/][Internet censorship and OONI]]: Jake Edge covers Tor's OONI project for detecting network interference — crowdsourced censorship measurement via ooni-probe framework; found blocked Palestinian news sites and T-Mobile WebGuard overblocking; open methodology vs Google's closed Transparency Report.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/495987/][Linux Format censored over 'Learn to Hack' feature (bit-tech)]]: Brief note that Barnes & Noble pulled Linux Format issue 154 over "Learn to Hack" Metasploit cover feature; TuxRADAR published article online; debate on "hacker" vs "cracker" terminology and private retailer censorship rights.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494463/][Quantum random numbers]]: Jake Edge covers ANU's Quantum Random Number Generator — 5.7 Gbit/s from quantum vacuum fluctuations, fastest RNG in world; hardware RNGs overrated: 256 bits of entropy sufficient for cryptography when fed through cryptographic PRNG (AES can do 713 MB/s); no HTTPS yet means man-in-the-middle could intercept; Lua used in entropy daemon.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494035/][Android trojan steals keystrokes using phone movements (ars technica)]]: TapLogger proof-of-concept app uses accelerometer/gyroscope/orientation sensors to infer keystrokes; fix proposals: disable sensors during sensitive input, split permissions for background sensor access, randomized keypad layouts; discussion on capability-based security model.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/493533/][An Interview With Linus Torvalds (TechCrunch)]]: TechCrunch interview covering quiet computers, desktop building, Linux advocacy; Linus prefers silent workstations; community discussion on fanless PCs, mini-ITX builds, Antec P180/P280 cases, ThinkPad thinkfan control, water cooling, SSD-only systems.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494388/][git.kernel.org mirror at Google]]: Google now mirrors kernel.org at kernel.googlesource.com — uses JGit with BigTable storage, smart HTTP protocol only, no rsync; mirror polls git:// every 30 min for consistency; SSL latency ~400ms, modified Git protocol helper to reuse SSL connections planned for git.git's contrib/.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494028/][O_HOT and O_COLD]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Ted Ts'o's proposal for O_HOT/O_COLD file creation flags to hint filesystem about data access frequency; ext4 implements by placing hot files in low-numbered blocks; criticism: unclear semantics, 'hotness' varies within files, different policies per filesystem, should let OS observe access patterns vs developers guessing.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494158/][Toward a safer fput()]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Al Viro's fput() locking solution — rename old fput() to fput_nodefer(), new fput() defers work asynchronously via task_work_add(); IMA appraisal extension deadlock problem; task_work_add() runs work before returning to user space ensuring close() semantics preserved; ~6 architectures need patches for task_work_add().
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494252/][A library for seccomp filters]]: Jake Edge covers libseccomp by Paul Moore — API for BPF-based seccomp mode 2; seccomp_init(), seccomp_rule_add(), seccomp_load(), seccomp_release(); actions: SCMP_ACT_KILL, SCMP_ACT_TRAP, SCMP_ACT_ERRNO, SCMP_ACT_TRACE; arg filtering with SCMP_A0-SCMP_A5 macros; LGPLv2.1 license; used by vsftpd 3.0.0 and Chromium.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/493411/][An Alternative Reading of the IADB Study on Peru's OLPC Implementation (OLPC News)]]: Oscar Becerra (former Peruvian Ministry of Education) responds to Economist criticism — OLPC primary goal was improving children's lives via 21st century tools, not test scores; Table 5 shows dramatic increase in computer access/use; Table 7 shows better cognitive skills; better tools for future vs immediate test improvement.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494265/][Android Cookbook--New from O'Reilly Media]]: New O'Reilly book by Ian Darwin — 200+ recipes crowdsourced from AndroidCookbook.com; covers UI controls, multitouch, layouts, multimedia, camera, GPS, web services; BlackBerry now accepts Android apps; worked example-driven approach for experienced Java developers moving to Android.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494500/][FreeBSD Device Drivers--New from No Starch Press]]: New No Starch Press book by Joseph Kong (author of Designing BSD Rootkits) — guide to FreeBSD driver development; covers Newbus framework, ISA/PCI/USB buses, DMA, interrupt handling; practical chapters on parallel port, USB printer, Intel Gigabit Ethernet drivers; CAM for HBAs.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494502/][Using Drupal, 2nd Edition--New from O'Reilly Media]]: New O'Reilly book on Drupal 7 by Angela Byron, Addison Berry, Bruno De Bondt — project-based chapters with step-by-step recipes; covers Drupal concepts, building blocks, configuration; new modules including Drupal Commerce, Media, Workbench; aimed at beginners through experienced developers.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494499/][LoMus 2012]]: Fourth edition of libre music software competition — search for open-source software for musical/intermedia creation; submission deadline April 29; awards ceremony May 11 at JIM 2012; prizes for innovative open-source audio/music software.

-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494491/][Wendy Seltzer to Keynote Ohio LinuxFest 2012]]: Wendy Seltzer (W3C Policy Counsel, Harvard Berkman Fellow) to keynote Ohio LinuxFest September 2012 — founded Chilling Effects Clearinghouse; board of Tor Project; works on copyright, trademark, patent, open source, privacy issues.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492859/][LFCS 2012: The Linux System Definition]]: Jake Edge covers OIN CEO Keith Bergelt at Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit — OIN patents now cover 1800 packages (expanded from 1100); 440+ licensees; defensive publications against bad patents; Google/IBM/OIN Code Search for prior art; Microsoft using 25 patents to attack mobile Linux; Tizen/webOS/MeeGo add resilience.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492624/][LFCS 2012: The future of GLIBC]]: Jake Edge covers Carlos O'Donell and Roland McGrath at LFCS — GLIBC moving to consensus-driven self-governance; dissolved steering committee; libc-alpha moderation removed; 25-30 committers; C11 atomic operations coming in 2.16; libm almost complete; TIRPC split; EGLIBC merger discussions; testing framework needs work; long-term: tracing support, auto-generated libm, exception-less syscalls.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492959/][Allocating uninitialized file blocks]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Zheng Liu's FALLOC_FL_NO_HIDE_STALE flag for fallocate() — marks blocks as initialized without writing zeros; benchmark: 76s to 18s for random-write workload; security concerns (sysctl default off, CAP_SYS_RAWIO); Ric Wheeler calls it security hole; alternative: background scrubber process; ext4 vs XFS performance comparison.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492125/][Toward more reliable logging]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Kay Sievers' structured printk() patch — record-oriented log buffer with sequence numbers; printk_emit() for dictionary KEY=value pairs; /dev/kmsg now supports read/poll; format: priority,seq,time;message\nSUBSYSTEM=...\nDEVICE=...; Linus suggested splitting record format for 3.4 merge; discussion on lumberjack/CEE/JSON structured logging standards.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492296/][LTTng 2.0: Tracing for power users and developers - part 2]]: Mathieu Desnoyers et al. — combined kernel/user-space tracing with lttng-ust; performance counter calibration with kretprobes; LTTngTop ncurses tool for trace analysis; flight recorder snapshots; live trace streaming in development; use cases: interrupt handler timing, fsync bottlenecks, distributed filesystem cache sizing.
-  [[https://lwn.net/Articles/493164/][(deferred) bits from the DPL: March 2012]]: Stefano Zacchiroli's Debian Project Leader report — 5-year hardware replacement plan (9k/year); Debian accepted for Google Summer of Code; DEP-5 (debian/copyright format) ACCEPTED; trademark guidelines for encumbered software; DuckDuckGo revenue sharing; .debian.net domains opened; Debian 7 (Wheezy) freeze upcoming.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492624/][LFCS 2012: The future of GLIBC]]: Jake Edge covers Carlos O'Donell and Roland McGrath at LFCS — GLIBC moving to consensus-driven self-governance; dissolved steering committee; libc-alpha moderation removed; 25-30 committers; C11 atomic operations coming in 2.16; libm almost complete; TIRPC split; EGLIBC merger discussions; testing framework needs work; long-term: tracing support, auto-generated libm, exception-less syscalls.
