- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492138/][Langley: False Start's Failure]]: Jake Edge covers Adam Langley explaining why Google ended its False Start SSL experiment — hardware SSL terminators caused issues; scheme required internet-wide scanning to build blacklist of problematic sites; Google ending support after list erosion; False Start still works with SPDY servers using NPN; discussion of SSL warnings, certificate verification, self-signed certs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492885/][The H Speed Guide to Lua]]: ris covers The H's Lua programming language guide — 20k lines of ANSI C, 182KB memory footprint; register-based VM with bytecode; incremental garbage collection; designed for embedding; LuaJIT2 supports x86, x86-64, ARM, PPC, MIPS; coroutines from C unparalleled; debate on 1-based arrays, indentation syntax vs braces, lack of regex vs patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492714/][PHP: a fractal of bad design]]: Jake Edge covers Eevee's detailed criticism of PHP — 'virtually every feature is broken'; predictability, consistency, reliability, debuggability, security issues; comparison to BASIC's mental mutilation; extensive discussion on language design, competence, C vs Perl predictability, sequence points, undefined behavior.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492955/][Head First C]]: O'Reilly Media press release for new C programming book by David Griffiths — brain-friendly guide covering language basics, pointers, dynamic memory, multi-threading, network programming; C as entry point to understanding computers; suitable as college textbook.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491555/][Bug reports: information or spam?]]: Nathan Willis covers Debian bug tracking debate — Welle's bug rejected for blacklisted URL (foo.org on uribl); RFC 2606 example domains suggested; spam filters vs user experience; Debian BTS email-only reporting limitations; reportbug tool; discussion on SMTP blocking, HTTP fallback, air-gapped networks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491258/][LFCS 2012: The kernel panel]]: Jake Edge covers kernel panel at LFCS — Greg KH moderating; panelists: Mel Gorman (memory management), John Linville (wireless), James Bottomley (SCSI), Keith Packard (graphics); topics: NUMA migration schemes, containers/cgroups, 802.11ac, X vs Wayland, stable kernel releases, structured logging, SCSI future, bufferbloat, Android patches, power measurement, hardware bypass.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491440/][SELinuxDenyPtrace and security by default]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Fedora 17's SELinuxDenyPtrace feature — ptrace() allows any program to inspect other processes owned by same user; feature denies ptrace by default; broke gdb, strace, DrKonqi; debate over security vs convenience; Ubuntu uses Yama module; discussion on user vs program privileges, Android's per-app UID model, capabilities for binaries.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491516/][Remote root hole in Samba]]: Samba security releases 3.6.4, 3.5.14, 3.4.16 fix CVE-2012-1182 — PIDL-based autogenerated code allowed overwriting beyond allocated array; remote code execution as root; bug in IDL compiler; existed since ~2007; discussion on managed languages vs C, bounds checking, fat pointers, chroot jails.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490855/][AT&T Microcell FAIL]]: FailOverflow analysis of AT&T 3G femtocell — runs Busybox/Linux; hardcoded backdoor called 'BackdoorPacketCmdLine'; UDP packets execute commands via backticksh; port globally accessible; encouraged placed behind NAT; UPnP hole punching concerns; 3G femtocells generally rootable; GPL questions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490973/][Wheeler: Insecure open source software libraries?]]: David Wheeler blog post — bundled libraries lose security advantage of OSS since fixes aren't used; developers don't update embedded libs; distributions ship old versions; Google Chromium bundles; discussion on library stability, API compatibility, distribution patching, games bundling SDL/ogg.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491716/][A new security subsystem wiki]]: Kernel.org wiki down after breakin; kernel security developers created kernsec.org wiki; also btrfs wiki moved to btrfs.ipv5.de; discussion of redirecting old wiki.kernel.org addresses.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491722/][SCHED_DEADLINE returns]]: Jonathan Corbet covers deadline scheduling patches — processes declare max CPU time and deadline; scheduler ensures deadlines met; new developer Juri Lelli maintaining; git repo, test app, mailing list; WCET (worst-case execution time) hard to determine; priority inheritance patches still need work.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491310/][A new approach to user namespaces]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Eric Biederman's user namespace patches — kuid_t/kgid_t types to separate kernel IDs from namespace IDs; prevents mixing errors; make_kuid(), from_kuid(), from_kuid_munged() functions; uid_map setup via /proc; container root can set up sub-namespaces; CAP_SETUID privilege; makes containers more secure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491653/][Finding the right evolutionary niche]]: Neil Brown on Android's 'timed gpio' driver for vibrators — Android added separate driver vs modifying existing; examined gpio, leds, input subsystems; input force-feedback framework provides 'rumble' with fail-safe timer; reassigning vibrator functionality; highlights need for persistence when finding right kernel niche.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491510/][LTTng 2.0: Tracing for power users and developers - part 1]]: Mathieu Desnoyers et al. introduce LTTng 2.0 tracer — rewrite of 0.x; works on vanilla kernels 2.6.38+; combined kernel and user-space tracing; CTF (Common Trace Format); multi-user, multiple sessions; Babeltrace converter; comparison with Perf and Ftrace; installation on Ubuntu 12.04.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491237/][The state of Wayland]]: Brief summary of Wayland status — GTK+ 3.4.1 and Qt5 have complete Wayland support except CSD; EFL and Clutter complete support; applications need toolkit support not Xlib; discussion on remote Wayland (vncserver), xpra, SPICE, input redirection, window management API.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491075/][A report from the Peru OLPC deployment]]: Economist summary of IDB report on Peru OLPC — no improvement in math/reading; positive impacts on computer skills; cognitive abilities from programs aimed at thinking processes; high-quality instruction still needed; discussion on Khan Academy, Sugata Mitra's Hole in the Wall, Uruguay/Paraguay success vs Peru failures.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491515/][Linux for Your Electric Car]]: Tumanako Project — open source EV drive package and inverter for 200kW induction motor; 6 months to full open source; SPICE inversion mentioned; developer Philip Court.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491560/][Build Awesome Command-Line Applications in Ruby]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf press release — David Copeland's book on Ruby CLI apps; self-documenting, robust, adaptable; free open source parsers; defaults for simple use; man pages and help; testing CLI apps.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490457/][Why bother supporting ARM?]]: Jonathan Corbet on Fedora ARM as primary architecture — ARM messy with many vendors; lack of hardware discoverability; no binary blobs policy; device tree consolidation; ARM slower for builds; ARM dominant in mobile Linux; Fedora criteria for architecture promotion; disruptive technology dilemma for Red Hat.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490516/][An update on Oracle v. Google]]: Adam Saunders covers Oracle vs Google trial (April 16) — Java copyright/patent infringement; Google used clean room implementation; most Oracle patents rejected via reexamination; only '104 (JIT) and '520 (static init) remain; API copyright claim weak (Baker v. Selden); Android code no longer in Android; FSF argues GPL Java should have been used; Android under threat from Apple, Microsoft patents too.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490291/][Runtime filesystem consistency checking]]: Jake Edge covers 'Recon' system from University of Toronto — runtime consistency checking instead of offline fsck; global invariants transformed to local; ext3 has 33 invariants checked at transaction commit; sits between filesystem and block layer; caught errors fsck missed; 2% I/O overhead; performance impact modest; comparison to lockdep.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490518/][Libsecret revealed]]: Nathan Willis covers Stef Walter's libsecret library — replaces libgnome-keyring; thread-safe, introspectable, async; full Secret Service API over D-Bus; works with GNOME and KDE secret services; simple password API + complete API; Python/JavaScript examples; migration for GNOME 3.6.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490394/][OSADL on realtime Linux determinism]]: OSADL press release — year of latency testing on PREEMPT_RT kernels; 730+ latency plots per system; AMD Athlon, ARM OMAP, MIPS Loongson, Intel Atom, VIA C7 tested; absence of outliers demonstrates generic deterministic behavior; 100 µs vs 50 µs differences across kernel versions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490413/][Udev and systemd to merge]]: Kay Sievers announces udev merging into systemd — udev 45 jumps to systemd 184; built from same source tree; separate binaries (udevd, systemd); compatible with non-systemd init; libudev API untouched; reduces code duplication; separate builds for outside-systemd (initrd support); discussion on feature bloat, Zawinski's Law.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/489480/][Grinberg: Linux on an 8-bit micro?]]: Dmitry Grinberg wrote ARM emulator for ATmega1284p — 2 hours to boot to bash, 4 more for full Ubuntu; effective speed 6.5KHz; SD card formatting possible; hand-soldered board; extreme example of emulation overhead; discussion on earliest Unix machines, Minix, ELKS, Z80 UZI.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/448499/][The platform device API]]: Jonathan Corbet; platform devices for non-discoverable hardware; platform_driver struct; probe/remove callbacks; platform_device_register(); platform data; struct resource; memory/IRQ resources; i2c-gpio example; struct platform_device_id.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/448502/][Platform devices and device trees]]: Jonathan Corbet; device trees; board files proliferation problem; ARM/SoC systems; device tree compiler (dtc); Grant Likely; struct of_device_id; compatible property; of_get_property(); of_get_mac_address(); Open Firmware; device tree source (dts) vs binary (dtb).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/448692/][Making static analysis easier]]: Jonathan Corbet; static analysis tools; Stanford Checker/Coverity; GCC plugins; Mozilla Dehydra/Treehydra JavaScript; GCC MELT (Lisp-like); David Malcolm gcc-python-plugin; LLVM clang static analyzer; splint/sparse/BLAST; Cppcheck; Coccinelle; KLEE; Frama-C.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/448152/][Keeping the Desktop Dream Alive (LinuxInsider)]]: Jim Zemlin Linux Foundation interview; fragmentation vs efficient market; kernel multibillion-dollar investment; Android/Samsung TV/Facebook/NYSE; freedesktop.org problems; KDE vs GNOME fragmentation; Phonon audio abstraction; PulseAudio; packaging formats; app bundles; LSB standards.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/448654/][Keeping the Desktop Dream Alive, Part 2 (TechNewsWorld)]]: Jim Zemlin continued; smart grid power metering; 15-minute polling; 12 million customers; energy allocation; high-performance computing; Linux #1 or fastest-growing OS; embedded systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/448709/][HTML5 & CSS3 For The Real World]]: SitePoint book announcement; Estelle Weyl/Louis Lazaris/Alexis Goldstein; HTML5 video/audio/SVG/canvas; CSS3 web fonts/shadows/form gradients; @font-face; self-validating web forms; mobile web apps; geolocation/offline APIs; browser compatibility.
